METRO CABLE ANNOUNCEMENT:
This meeting of the Sacramento Metropolitan Fire District is recorded. The recording will be
cablecast on Metro Cable Channel 14, the local government affairs channel on the Comcast
and DirecTV U-Verse cable systems. The recording will also be closed captioned and video
streamed at metro14Iive.saccounty.gov. Today's meeting replays at 2:00 p.m. on Sunday,
May 25, 2025, and again at 6:00 p.m. on Monday, May 26, 2025, on Metro Cable
Channel 14. Once posted, the recording of this meeting can be viewed on-demand at
youtube. coml metrocable 14.

PUBLIC OPPORTUNITY TO DISCUSS MATTERS OF PUBLIC INTEREST WITHIN
DISTRICT JURISDICTION INCLUDING ITEMS ON OR NOT ON AGENDA:
The Board of Directors of the Sacramento Metropolitan Fire District appreciates and
encourages public interest and welcomes questions and opinions at its meetings. Public
members wishing to address the Board are requested to first be recognized by the presiding
officer and identify themselves for the record. The presiding officer may, in the interest of
time and good order, limit the number of public member presentations. Speakers' comments
will be limited to three (3) minutes (Per Section 31 of the Board of Directors Policies and
Procedures).

In accordance with Section 31 of the Board of Directors Policies and Procedures, members
of the Public requesting their written comments be read into the meeting record must be
present or have a representative present to read their comments during the time allotted.

CONSENT ITEMS:
Matters of routine approval including but not limited to action summary minutes, referral of
issues to committee, committee referrals to the full Board, items that require yearly approval,
declaration of surplus equipment, and other consent matters. The Consent Agenda is acted
upon as one unit unless a Board member requests separate discussion and/or action.

FINANCE

   FY 25/26 POSITION REQUESTS:
   •   The Finance Division has been busy preparing next year's preliminary budget.
       As you're aware, the budget is comprised of three major components:
          o Wages and benefits,
          o Services and supplies
          o Capital projects.
           Highlights of some of the work happening in these areas:

           a. Wages and Benefits: For the purposes of the budget, wages and benefits
              include new position requests. As you will recall, a couple of meetings ago,· Jeff
              Frye did a presentation on the Position Request Forms and the associated
              process. Following that presentation, you provided two· directions to staff: the
              first was to stop the ·strategic planning effort and focus on this year's staffing
              needs. The second was to include labor in the discussions.

              Tonight, I want to update you on the process briefly and where we are. The
              Position Request Form was created to request new positions, consider
              reclassifications, or evaluate adjustments to compensation. Budget managers
              submitted requests for 69 positions. 30 of the positions are carryovers from FY
              24/25. The total estimated cost of these requests is approximately $18 million.

              Staff has met with Labor, and jointly we looked at the requests and prioritized
              them. As the process moves towards final recommendations for inclusion in the
              FY 25/26 budget there will be continued discussion, including additional PB

4.24.2025 Board Meetina Action Summarv Minutes                                    Page 3 of 6
                meetings with Labor, that will lead up to the preliminary budget presentation to
                the Finance Committee on May 22nd and a full budget presentation being made
                to the Board on June 12th.

             b. Services and Supplies: The Executive Team has  \
                                                                 met with all of the budget
                officers, and the finance team is compiling the budget requests for further
                discussion.

             c. Capital Projects: At the Last Board meeting, Jeff and Erin presented the
                preliminary capital project list. Now, the focus will turn to preparing the legal
                documents for the first Measure O bond issuance. The project team has been
                assembled, and they continue to move forward with the process.

BOARD MEMBER QUESTIONS AND COMMENTS

Director Rice stated that something that has really struck him over the last two years is that
all the staff that has come before us have nothing but positive things to say about the crews
they lead, and that sets a great tone. Director Rice and ,President Wood requested that staff
bring a presentation to the next Board meeting on the unsecured mental health calls, we
need staff to come up with a solution.

Director Clark thanked the men and women of Metro Fire and congratulated Fire Marshal
Amy Nygren on her promotion.

Director Goold asked when we can expect to expand some services that wellness, health,
and safety provide to our members' families. Would like to do my annual call out to someone
who has deep pockets who can sponsor all 80 of the kids that will come to fire camp,
especially to those who cannot afford it. I'm completely behind Director Rice on the mental
health call responses, and I'm worried about those calls going wrong. Also, how much are
we discussing this with our communities? I have full faith that we have great people involved,
and maybe we need the support of the community behind us.

Director Wood welcomed the new hires and congratulated Fire Marshal Amy Nygren on her
promotion. The Firefighters Burn Institute has a huge fundraising event called Luau on the
Links on Saturday, May 31, 2025, at The Pavilion at Haggin Oaks, and they need volunteers.
Please go to https://ffburn.org/ for more information and to purchase tickets.             p1o

Cyber Security Manager, no reportable action. 2. 91 O Claim of Brandy Scott v. Sacramento

 DATE:                May 22, 2025

 TO:                  Board of Directors

 SUBJECT:             Disclosure of material expenditure - Insurance Broker Services - USI Insurance
                      Services - $50,000

                                                                                                                             /
                                                           TOPIC

 Disclosure of material expenditure to purchase insurance brokerage services for the fiscal year
 ending June 30, 2026.

                                                        SUMMARY

 Staff will be expending funds to purchase Insurance Brokerage Services. The expenditure will
 be payable to USI in the amount of $50,000 for insurance brokerage services.

                                                       DISCUSSION

 USI Insurance Service provides Insurance Brokerage Services. Services include risk
 management, marketing, day-to-day consulting on servicing of insurance, claims services, and
 risk engineering services. For the fiscal year 2025/2026, USI brokered the District's commercial
 insurance package.

                                                     FISCAL IMPACT

 The fiscal impact is $50,000. Funds sufficient to meet this obligation are budgeted in the
 Preliminary Budget for 2025/2026.

                                                   RECOMMENDATION

 9taff recommends that the Board of Directors authorize the payment of $50,000 to USI
 Insurance Services for insurance brokerage services.

ADAM A. HOUSE
  Fire Chief


 DATE:          May 22, 2025

 TO:            Board of Directors

 SUBJECT:       Disclosure of material expenditure - Aviation Liability Insurance - Chubb
                Insurance Group - $185,187.00.

                                                 TOPIC

 Disclosure of material expenditure to purchase aviation liability insurance for the fiscal year
 ending June 30, 2026.

                                              SUMMARY

  Staff will be expending funds to purchase aviation liability insurance. The expenditure will be
  payable to Chubb Insurance Group in the amount of $185,187.00 for the aviation policy.

                                             DISCUSSION

  USI Insurance Services provided the District's insurance brokerage services this year and
  managed the marketing of the District's aviation liability insurance. The aviation liability
  insurance package for the upcoming fiscal year includes coverage for three flying helicopters
  and one grounded helicopter.

 The aviation policy premium has remained the same as in FY 24/25. We will be insuring three
 flying helicopters, each valued at $1,500,000, and one grounded helicopter valued at $350,000.
 The flying helicopters carry $10,000,000 of liability, and the grounded helicopter carries
 $1,000,000 of liability.

 The insurance requested includes any pilot approved by Metro Fire's Chief Pilot or designee
 and covers all uses in connection with the operations of Metro Fire including mutual aid
 agreements. Many carriers were solicited to provide a quote for the District's Aviation Insurance
 and all except Chubb Insurance Group declined. Chuob Insurance Group is the carrier
 recommended by USI to carry the District's aviation liability insurance needs.

                                           FISCAL IMPACT

 The fiscal impact is $185,187.00. Funds sufficient to meet this obligation are budgeted in the
 Preliminary Budget for FY 2025/2026.

                                        RECOMMENDATION

 Staff recommends that the Board of Directors authorize the payment of $185,187.00 to Chubb
 Insurance Group for the purchase of Aviation Liability Insurance.

ADAM A. HOUSE
  Fire Chief

     DATE:           May 22, 2025
     TO:             Board of Directors
     SUBJECT:        Qualified Bidders List - Fire Station 67 Project

                                               TOPIC
     Request to adopt a resolution establishing a Qualified Bidders List for the Fire Station 67
     Project.

                                               BACKGROUND
     On March 27, 2025, the Sacramento Metropolitan Fire District's (District) Board of Directors
     (Board) determined it was in the best interest of the District to ensure that potential bidders on
     the Project are qualified and responsible, and adopted Resolution 25-017 to establish a pre-
     qualification system for the Project, pursuant to Public Contract Code Section 20101 et seq.

                                                DISCUSSION
     On March 28, 2025, the District issued Request for Qualifications (RFQ) 25-03 for the purpose
     of pre-qualifying potential bidders for the Project and establishing a Qualified Bidders List. The
     District received 23 submittals in response to the RFQ. Three (3) responses did not conform to
     the submittal requirements, and were deemed non-responsive. Three (3) other responses did
     not meet the minimum scoring requirements and were disqualified. The remaining 17 submittals
     met the minimum requirements for pre-qualification.

     Based on the determinations of the pre-qualification process, staff recommends that the
     following firms be added to a Qualified Bidders List for the Project:
     Arntz Builders, Inc.           DL Falk Construction, Inc.                Rodan Builders, Inc.
     Bobo Construction, Inc.        F&H Construction                          Roebbelen Contracting, Inc.
     Broward Builders, Inc.         Gilbane Building Company                  Swinerton Builders
     Carter-Kelly, Inc.             Landmark Constructors, Inc.               Thompson Builders Corp.
     DG Granade, Inc.               Lathrop Construction Assoc, Inc.          Zovich & Sons, Inc.
     Diede Construction, Inc.       Otto Construction

                                              FISCAL IMPACT
     There is no fiscal impact for establishing the Qualified Bidders List.

                                        RECOMMENDATION
     Staff recommends that the Board adopt a resolution to establish a Qualified Bidders List that
     includes those firms who were successful in the pre-qualification process.

     Submitted by:


     i&i~
     Erin Castleberry
     Administrative Analyst                                ~-:.•;~~JDeve
                                                           J   ~         Iopment Officer

     ATTACHMENT:        Resolution Establishing a Qualified Bidders List for the Fire Station 67 Project

ADAM A. HOUSE
  Fire Chief

                                RESOLUTION NO. 2025-XXX

     A RESOLUTION OF THE SACRAMENTO METROPOLITAN FIRE DISTRICT
            ESTABLISHING A QUALIFIED BIDDERS LIST FOR THE
                       FIRE STATION 67 PROJECT
          WHEREAS, the Sacramento Metropolitan Fire District ("District") is a political subdivision
  of the State of California ("State") and is duly organized and existing pursuant to the State
  constitution and laws; and

ADAM A. HOUSE
  Fire Chief




 DATE:          May 22, 2025

 TO:            Board of Directors

 SUBJECT:       Special Fire Tax - Sloughhouse/Rancho Murieta Area



                                                TOPIC

  Board action is required in order to authorize Sacramento County to collect the District's
  Special Fire Tax in the Slough house/Rancho Murieta area for fiscal year 2025/26.



                                          BACKGROUND

 Under provisions of the California Constitution, the residents of the Slough house/Rancho
 Murieta area approved in November 2000, by more than a two-to-one margin, a special
 tax to help pay for the fire protection, prevention and training services in their community.
 The Special Fire Tax, initiated to replace the Fire Suppression Assessment Fee in place
 in the area since 1986, was capped at a maximum of $100 per parcel.


                                            DISCUSSION

  The County Assessor cannot levy nor collect the District's Special Fire Tax in the
  Sloughhouse/Rancho Murieta area without formal annual authorization from the District.
  To have the Special Fire Tax placed on the tax rolls, the Board must adopt a resolution
  authorizing the County Assessor to make the levy.

  The District has contracted with local agency financial consulting company NBS to assist
  with the administration of the Sloughhouse/Rancho Murieta Special Fire Tax, and they
  have estimated that the tax will generate $347,500 in revenues for fiscal year 2025/26.




                              Serving Sacramento and Placer Counties

                                                                                                                  P17
Page 2



                                     FISCAL IMPACT

Absent formal authorization from the District's Board, the County Assessor cannot levy
the Special Fire Tax in the Sloughhouse/Rancho Murieta area. Failure to assess the fee
will result to a loss of revenues of approximately $347,500 to fund fire protection services
in that area.


                                  RECOMMENDATION

Staff recommends adoption of the resolution authorizing the County Assessor to
incorporate the $100 per parcel Special Fire Tax for the Sloughhouse/Rancho Murieta
area with the 2025/26 Sacramento County property tax levy.




Submitted by:




Dave O'Toole
Chief Financial Officer



Approved by:

damA.House

                                        RESOLUTION NO. 2025-XXX

                  A RESOLUTION TO COLLECT A SPECIAL TAX AUTHORIZED IN
                THE SLOUGHHOUSE /RANCHO MURIETA AREA AND TO AUTHORIZE
                     THE COUNTY TO COLLECT THE FUNDS FOR FY 2025/26

              WHEREAS, the electorate of the Sacramento Metropolitan Fire District passed a Special
       Tax for fire operating expenses in the Sloughhouse/Rancho Murieta Area; and

              WHEREAS, the Special Tax authorization is adopted pursuant to Article XIIIC, Section
       2(d) of the California Constitution; and

              WHEREAS, the purpose of the Special Tax is to establish a stable source of
       supplementary funds to acquire, operate, and maintain fire suppression equipment and
       services, or for the purpose of paying the salaries and benefits of firefighting personnel, or both,
       whether or not these services are actually used; and

             WHEREAS, on November 7, 2000, the residents of the Sloughhouse/Rancho Murieta
       Area voted on and successfully passed Measure Q by a yes vote of 2,100 and a no vote of
       872; and

             WHEREAS, the Board of Directors of the Sacramento Metropolitan Fire District now
       agrees to collect the Special Tax for this 2025/26 fiscal year.

               NOW, THEREFORE, BE IT .RESOLVED that the Sacramento Metropolitan Fire District
       authorizes the Sacramento County Office of Auditor/Controller to collect these funds for the
       District from an estimated 3,475 parcels at $100.00 each for an approxmate levy amount of
       $347,500.

ADAM A. HOUSE
  Fire Chief




  DATE:         May 22, 2025

  TO:           Board of Directors

  SUBJECT:      Annual Adjustment for Medical Aid and Ambulance Transport User
                Fee


                                            TOPIC

  Ordinance #2023-01 (the Ordinance), which was adopted by the Board of Directors
  on June 22, 2023, provides for an annual increase in the District's Medical Aid and
  Ambulance Transport User Fees.


                                      BACKGROUND

  In order to keep pace with annual cost inflation, the Ordinance specifies that the
  fees identified in Exhibit "A" of the Ordinance shall be adjusted annually, beginning
  July 1, 2024, and each July 1 thereafter. The amount of change shall be based on
  the percentage change in the Consumer Price Index (CPI) Series Title Medical
  Care in the U.S. City Average, All Urban Consumers, Not Seasonally Adjusted, as
  published by the U.S. Department of Labor, Bureau of Labor Statistics (the Medical
  CPI) for the twelve (12) month period ending December 31 of the preceding
  calendar year. The Ordinance also states that approval by the Board of Directors
  shall be by resolution, adopted at a regularly scheduled meeting of the Board prior
  to the enactment of the increase. The effective date of the increase would be July
  1, 2025.


                                        DISCUSSION

   Based on the percentage change in the annual Medical CPI for calendar year 2024
   compared to calendar year 2025, the percentage fee adjustment change effective
   July 1, 2025 will be 2.84%. The current and recommended fees are shown in the
   table on the next page.                                                •




                            Serving Sacramento and Placer Counties

                                                                                                    P20
Page2


                                                    Current         Recommended

           Emergency Ambulance Transport
           Base Rate                                    $2,793             $2,872

           First Responder Fee                                502             516
           Assessment at Scene                                502             516
           Oxygen                                             179             184
           Night Charge                                       159             164
           Cardiac Monitor                                    139             143
           Mileage                                             50              51


                                      FISCAL IMPACT

        It is estimated that the recommended fee adjustments will result in additional
        District cost recovery of approximately $200,000 during FY 2025/26.          •


                                    RECOMMENDATION

        In accordance with the Ordinance, staff recommends adoption of the attached
        resolution amending the Ambulance Fee Schedule.



        Submitted by:



        B-l1~
        Chief Financial Officer




        Assistant Chief, EMS

  Fire Chief                         RESOLUTION NO. 2025-XXX

           A RESOLUTION OF THE SACRAMENTO METROPOLITAN FIRE DISTRICT
        APPROVING AN ADJUSTMENT TO THE FEE SCHEDULE FOR MEDICAL AID AND
             AMBULANCE TRANSPORT SERVICES PROVIDED BY THE DISTRICT

         WHEREAS, the Sacramento Metropolitan Fire District ("District") is a political subdivision of
  the State of California ("State") and is duly organized and existing pursuant to the State constitution
  and laws; and
        WHEREAS, on June 22, 2023, the District adopted Ordinance 2023-01, an ordinance
  amending the fee schedule for medical aid and ambulance transport user fees; and

          WHEREAS, Ordinance 2023-01 provides for annual adjustment of fees , beginning July 1,
  2024 and each July 1 thereafter, based on the change in the Consumer Price Index Series Title
  Medical Care in the U.S. City Average, All Urban Consumers, Not Seasonally Adjusted (i.e., Medical
  CPI), subject to Board of Directors approval by resolution; and

          WHEREAS, the change in the Medical CPI, as published by the U.S. Department of Labor,
   Bureau of Labor Statistics, for the 12-month period ending December 31, 2024 was 2.84%; and

          WHEREAS , it remains the intent of the District to provide medical aid and ambulance
   transport services within the District.

           NOW, THEREFORE, BE IT RESOLVED, the Board of Directors hereby approves the 2.84%
   increase effective July 1, 2025 in all medical aid and ambulance transport services, as set forth in
   the attached Exhibit "A" and directs that the fees shall be uniformly applied and collected.

ADAM A. HOUSE
   Fire Chief




  DATE:         May 22, 2025

  TO:           Board of Directors

  SUBJECT: Annual Fee Adjustment for Operational Permits, Plan Review, New
           Construction Inspections, General Fire and Life Safety Inspections,
           and Other Miscellaneous Services


                                            TOPIC

  Ordinance #2023"02 (the Ordinance), which was adopted by the Board of Directors
  on July 27, 2023, provides for an annual increase in the fee collected for
  operational permits, plan review, new construction inspections, general fire and life
  safety inspections, and other miscellaneous services. The effective date of the
  next increase will be July 1, 2025.


                                      BACKGROUND

  In order to keep pace with annual cost inflation, the Ordinance specifies that the
  fees ide_ ntified in Exhibit A of the Ordinance shall be adjusted annually, beginning
  July 1, 2024, and each July 1 thereafter. The amount of change shall be based on
  the percentage change in the Consumer Price Index (CPI) Consumer Price Index
  for all urban consumers, not seasonally adjusted, for the area of San Francisco-
  Oakland"Hayward, CA, as published by the U.S. Department of Labor, Bureau of
  Labor Statistics for the twelve (12) month period ending April 30 of the current
  calendar year. The Ordinance also states that approval by the Board of Directors
  shall be by resolution, adopted at a regularly scheduled meeting of the Board prior
  to the enactment of the increase.


                                       DISCUSSION

  Based on the percentage change in the annual CPI for twelve"month period ended
  April 30, 2025, the fee adjustment effective July 1, 2025 will be 1.27%. The current
  and recommended fees are shown in Exhibit A attached to the proposed
  resolution.




                            Serving Sacramento and Placer Counties

                                                                                                    P24
Page2




                                        FISCAL IMPACT

         It is estimated that the recommended fee adjustments will result in 'additional
         District cost recovery of approximately $80,000 during FY 2025/26.


                                     RECOMMENDATION

         In accordance with the Ordinance, staff recommends adoption of the attached
         resolution amending the fee schedule.

        A RESOLUTION OF THE SACRAMENTO METROPOLITAN FIRE DISTRICT

          WHEREAS, the Sacramento Metropolitan Fire District ("District") is a political
   subdivision of .the State of California ("State") and is duly organized and existing pursuant to
   the State constitution and laws; and                                                      "

          WHEREAS, on July 27, 2023, the District adopted Ordinance 2023-02, an
   ordinance amending the fee schedule for operational permits, plan review, new
   construction inspections, general fire and life safety inspections and other miscellaneous
   services; and

            WHEREAS, Ordinance 2023-02 provides for annual adjustment of fees, beginning
   July 1, 2024 and each July 1 thereafter, based on the change in the Consumer Price Index
   for all urban consumers, not seasonally adjusted, for the area of San Francisco-Oakland-
   Hayward, CA for the 12-month period ending April 30, subject to Board of Directors
   approval by resolution; and

         WHEREAS, the change in the aforementioned CPI, as published by the U.S.
   Department of Labor, Bureau of Labor Statistics, for the 12-month period ending April 30,
   2025 was 1.27%; and

           WHEREAS, it remains the intent of the District to provide operational permits, plan
   review, new construction inspections, general fire and life safety inspections, and other
   miscellaneous services within the District; and

           NOW, THEREFORE, BE IT RESOLVED, the Board of Directors hereby approves
   the 1.27% increase effective July 1, 2025 in all operational permits, plan review, new
   construction inspections, general fire and life safety inspections, and other miscellaneous
   services, as set forth in the attached Exhibit "A" and directs that the fees shall be uniformly
   applied and collected .

                                         RESOLUTION NO. 2025-XXX

   A RESOLUTION OF THE SACRAMENTO METROPOLITAN FIRE DISTRICT I.T.
                            EQUIPMENT

          WHEREAS, the Sacramento Metropolitan Fire District ("District") is a political
   subdivision of the State of California ("State") and is duly organized and existing pursuant
   to the State constitution and laws; and

         WHEREAS, the District's I.T. Division has old and unused capital assets that need
   to be E-Wasted; and

          WHEREAS, the district requires all resolution of capital assets to be presented
   to the board for approval to E-Waste.

         NOW THEREFORE BE IT RESOLVED that the Board of Directors of
   the Sacramento Metropolitan Fire District does hereby approve the resolution of IT
   equipment, as set forth in the attached Exhibit "A".

ADAM A, HOUSE
   Fire Chief


      DATE:           May 22, 2025

      TO:             Board of Directors

      SUBJECT:        Purchase Approval- Fleet Service Truck



                                                          TOPIC

      Staff seeks Board approval for the purchase of a Fleet Service Truck from National Auto Fleet Group.

                                                        SUMMARY

      This vehicle wlll be replacing a current Fleet Service Truck that Is at the end of Its service life due to age
      and mileage.

                                                       DISCUSSION

      The Sacramento Metropolitan Fire District (Metro Fire} Intends to fulfill this purchase utilizing the
      Sourcewell purchasing contract number 091521-NAF. Sourcewell Is a State of Minnesota local
      government unit and service cooperative that facilitates competitive publlc solicitation and contract award
      processes for the benefit of Its government and education participating entitles across the United States ·
      and Canada. Cooperative purchasing provides these participating entitles with Increased administrative
      efficiencies and the power of combined purchasing volume that result In overall cost savings. Metro Fire
      Is registered with Sourcewell as a participating entity and Is eligible to utilize this contract. The
      Purchasing Division has reviewed the contract and determined It Is consli,tent with Metro Fire purchasing
      policies and procedures.

                                                     FISCAL IMPACT

      The total cost of the purchase for the Fleet Service Truck Is $195,959.91. The funding for this purchase Is
      Included In the FY 2024/25 Midyear Budget.

                                                   RECOMMENDATION

      Staff respectfully recommends the Board approve the purchase of this Fleet Service Truck from National                 l

      Auto Fleet Group utilizing the Sourcewell contract number 091521-NAF.                                                  t

ADAM A. HOUSE
  Fire Chief


     DATE:         May 22, 2025

     TO:           Board of Directors

     SUBJECT:      Introduction and First Reading of proposed Ordinance No. 2025-01, To
                   Adopt the 2025 Fire Hazard Severity Zone Map as Recommended by the
                   California State Fire Marshal


                                                  TOPIC

     Introduction of Ordinance 2025-01, pursuant to Government Code Section 51179,
     whereas local agencies are required to adopt the fire hazard severity zone designations
     within 120 days of receiving the recommendations from the State Fire Marshal.


                                  BACKGROUND -OR-SUMMARY

      Government Code Section 51178 requires the California State Fire Marshal to identify
      and recommend areas within the state as moderate, high, or very high fire hazard
      severity zones based on consistent statewide criteria. On March 10, 2025, the District
      received the 2025 Fire Hazard Severity Zone (FHSZ) Map from the State Fire Marshal,
      identifying designated zones within District's jurisdiction.


                                              DISCUSSION

      The District has not reduced or altered the fire hazard severity designations established
      by the State Fire Marshal, and this adoption is consistent with the model ordinance
      requirements by the State Fire Marshal. The District finds that adoption of the map is in
      the interest of public safety, supports fire prevention and mitigation efforts, and ensures
      compliance with applicable state law.


                                            FISCAL IMPACT

      No fiscal impact.




                                    Serving Sacramento and Placer Counties
                                                                                                              P51
Page 2


                                           RECOMMENDATION

          Staff recommends that the District ~oard of Director's waive the first reading and
          introduce the proposed Ordinance by title only and proceed with scheduling the second
          reading for June 12, 2025, to adopt Ordinance No. 2025-01 thereby adopting the 2025
          Fire Hazard Severity Zone Map.

                                                           Approved by:



             Iana E. Schmidt
         _ (Acting) Deputy Fire Marshal


          ATTACHMENTS:

          Attachment 1: Ordinance No. 2025-01 with Exhibit A




                                     Serving Sacramento and Placer Counties

                                                                                                  P52
                                 ORDINANCE NO. 2025-01


AN ORDINANCE OF THE SACRAMENTO METROPOLITAN FIRE DISTRICT BOARD
 OF DIRECTORS ADOPTING THE 2025 FIRE HAZARD SEVERITY ZONE MAP AS
        RECOMMENDED BY THE CALIFORNIA STATE FIRE MARSHAL


        WHEREAS, Government Code Section 51178 requires the California State Fire Marshal
to identify and recommend areas within the state as moderate, high, or very high fire hazard
severity zones based on consistent statewide criteria; and

      WHEREAS, pursuant to Government Code Section 51179, local agencies are required to
adopt the fire hazard severity zone designations within 120 days of receiving the
recommendations from the State Fire Marshal; and

       WHEREAS, on March 10, 2025, Sacramento Metropolitan Fire District ("District") received
the 2025 Fire Hazard Severity Zone (FHSZ) Map from the State Fire Marshal, identifying
designated zones within District's jurisdiction; and

        WHEREAS, information regarding the 2025 FHSZ Maps on a state-wide and county-by-
county basis is available on the public website of the State Fire Marshal at
https://osfm.fire.ca.gov/what-we-do/community-wildfire-preparedness-and-mitigation/fire-hazard-
severity-zones

       WHEREAS, and the specific map for Sacramento Metropolitan Fire District is attached
and incorporated herein as Exhibit A, and is also available on the District's public website at:
www.MetroFire.ca.gov/fire-hazard-severity-zones

        WHEREAS, the District has made the proposed FHSZ Map available for public review,
provided proper public notice in accordance with Government Code Section 51179(9), and held
a public hearing on May 22, 2025 to receive public input; and

       WHEREAS, the District finds that adoption of the map is in the interest of public safety,
supports fire prevention and mitigation efforts, and ensures compliance with applicable state law;
and

        WHEREAS, the District has not reduced or altered the fire hazard severity designations
established by the State Fire Marshal, and this adoption is consistent with the model ordinance
requirements by the State Fire Marshal.

NOW, THEREFORE, THE BOARD OF DIRECTORS OF SACRAMENTO METROPOLITAN
FIRE DISTRICT ORDAINS AS FOLLOWS:

       Section 1. Adoption of 2025 FHSV Maps. The 2025 Fire Hazard Severity Zone Map for
       Sacramento County as recommended by the California State Fire Marshal for the District's
       service area is adopted without change and is incorporated herein as Exhibit A.

       Section 2. Effective Date. This Ordinance shall take effect and be in full force 30 days
       after its final passage and adoption at its second reading. After adoption, District Staff shall
       submit the Ordinance to State Board of Forestry and Fire Protection.


                                                                                                          P53
Ordinance No. 2025-01                                                                   Page 2 of3


       Section 3. Severability. The ordinance shall be liberally constructed to achieve its
       purpose and preserve its validity. If any provisions or clause of this ordinance or
       application thereof to any person or circumstance is held invalid, such invalidity shall not
       affect other provisions or applications of this ordinance which can be given effect without
       the valid provision or application. To this end, the provisions of this ordinance are declared
       to be servable and are intended to have independent validity.

of the Sacramento Metropolitan Fire District, held on the 22nd day of May, 2025, by the following

ADAM A. HOUSE
  Fire Chief


     DATE:

     TO:           Board of Directors

     SUBJECT:      Contract Award Recommendation - 9-1-1 Advanced Life Support
                   Ambulance Services

                                            TOPIC
     Staff requests the Board of Directors approve a contract award to American Medical
     Response West OBA American Medical Response (AMR) for 9-1-1 Advanced Life Support
     ambulance services.

                                          BACKGROUND
     The Sacramento Metropolitan Fire District (District) is dispatched by the Sacramento
     Regional Fire/EMS Communications Center (SRFECC) located in Sacramento, California.
     SRFECC has one of the highest call volumes of all dispatch centers in the United States,
     answering nearly 500,000 calls per year.

     The District's Emergency Medical Services (EMS) Division is responsible for the District's
     provision of emergency medical response services, including Advanced Life Support (ALS)
     and Basic Life Support (BLS) pre-hospital medical aid and ground emergency transport.
     These services are delivered through the strategic deployment of ALS-capable first
     responder units (engines, trucks, and squads) staffed with firefighter-paramedics; dual-role
     Fire Department Medic (FDM) ambulance units staffed with firefighter-paramedics; single-
     role Metro Medic Program (MMP) ambulance units staffed with paramedics and Emergency
     Medical Technicians (EMTs) (non-firefighter); and contracted third-party ALS ambulance
     units. Additional surge protection is also provided through contracted third-party ALS
     ambulance units to augment the EMS system during peak periods.
                                                                            I

     The District's existing contract with it's current contracted third-party 9-1-1 ALS ambulance
     service provider will be expiring on June 30, 2025.

                                            DISCUSSION
     On December 31, 2024, the District's Purchasing Division issued Request for Proposals
     (RFP) 24-07 to solicit proposals from qualified contractors to provide 9-1-1 ALS ambulance
     services as a supplemental service to Metro Fire's current ambulance and emergency
     medical services.

     The qualified contractor will be required to provide a minimum of ten (10) 12-hour ALS units,
     seven days per week (minimum of 43,800 unit hours per year). These contracted units must
     be ambulances dedicated to the 9-1-1 system and staffed with one Paramedic and one
     EMT or two Paramedics. Additionally, the contractor must guarantee their capacity to
     provide additional temporary units to surge into the 9-1 -1 system, at the District's request,


                                  Serving Sacramento and Placer Counties
                                                                                                             P64
Page 2


         during times of an acute increase in patient volume that has the potential to severely
         challenge or exceed the capacity of the local EMS System. Surge units may also be
         requested for temporary assignment to maintain service delivery during times of ambulance
         drawdown resulting in a reduction of available resources.

         The District received proposals through the District's e-procurement portal, OpenGov, from
         the following two firms:

            •    Falck Northern California Corp.
            •    American Medica l Response West OBA American Medical Response

         An evaluation committee comprised of two internal and two external members, all having
         exten_sive EMS experience, reviewed and scored the proposals using the following
         evaluation criteria:
             • Organizational Qualifications and Experience
             • Patient Care Approach
             • Resource Utilization and Adaptability
             • System Adaptability      '
             • Past Performance
             • Fee Proposal

         AMR was the highest scoring proposer.

                                                  FISCAL IMPACT
         This contract will be in effect for three years, beginning July 1, 2025, and may be extended
         for up to two additional 12-month periods. The fee proposal is as follows:
           ..                                                                    --
                                                         Unit Hourly           Minimum Total
                          Description
                                                            Cost                Annual Cost
                Year 1 - 911 Ambulance Services            $193.33                   $8,467,854.00
                Year 2 - 911 Ambulance Services            $202.99                   $8,890,962.00
                Year 3 - 911 Ambulance Services            $213.14                   $9,335,532.00
                Year 4 - 91 1 Ambulance Services           $224.87                   $9,849,306.00
                Year 5 - 911 Ambulance Services            $237.23                 $10,390,674.00

         EMS fees collected after the ambulance response are used to offset the contract cost.

                                        RECOMMENDATION
         Staff recommends the Board adopt a resolution to approve a contract award to American
         Medical Response West OBA American Medical Response and authorize the Fire Chief or
         his designee to execute and administer the attached agreement and any extensions
         thereto.




                                      Serving Sacramento and Placer Counties

                               RESOLUTION NO. 2025-XXX

     A RESOLUTION OF THE SACRAMENTO METROPOLITAN FIRE DISTRICT
       APPROVING A CONTRACT AWARD FOR ADVANCED LIFE SUPPORT
                        AMBULANCE SERVICES


          WHEREAS, the Sacramento Metropolitan Fire District ("District") is a political
   subdivision of the State of California ("State") and is duly organized and existing pursuant
   to the State constitution and laws; and

         WHEREAS, the District issued Request for Proposals ("RFP") 24-07 for the
   purpose of identifying and selecting a qualified firm to provide 9-1-1 Advanced Life
   Support ("ALS") ambulance services as a supplemental service to the District's current
   ambulance and Emergency Medical Services ("EMS"); and

         WHEREAS, the District received two responsive proposals in response to RFP 24-
   07; and

         WHEREAS, after an evaluation and scoring of the submittals received using the
   evaluation criteria listed in RFP 24-07, the District desires to award a contract for the
   performance of these services to American Medical Response West OBA American
   Medical Response ("AMR"), who was the highest scoring proposer.

        NOW THEREFORE BE IT RESOLVED that the Board of Directors of the
   Sacramento Metropolitan Fire District does hereby:

          1. Approve a contract award for Request for Proposals 24-07 Advanced Life
             Support Ambulance Services to American Medical Response West OBA
             American Medical Response.
          2. Authorize and delegate authority to the Fire Chief or his designee to negotiate,
             execute, and administer the agreement and any extension thereto.

         PASSED, APPROVED AND ADOPTED this 22 nd day of MAY 2025. I, MARNI

                         PROFESSIONAL SERVICES AGREEMENT

This Agreement, dated as of July 1, 2025 rEffective Date") is by and between the Sacramento
Metropolitan Fire District ("District"), and American Medical Response West OBA American
Medical Response ("Contractor") who are hereinafter collectively referred to as the "Parties".
The Agreement will be effective upon final execut ion by all parties and approval by the District's
Board of Directors.

                                            RECITALS

WHEREAS, the District issued Request for Proposals (~FP) 44-07 which solicited written proposals
for Advanced Life Support (ALS) Ambulance Services (Services); and

WHEREAS, the District sought to award a cqhtract for the Services based on the evaluation of
proposals received in response to RFP 24-07; and

WHEREAS, the District desires the ?ervices as more fvlly descr.ibed in Exhibits A here to, "Scope
of Services," from Contractor;

WHEREAS, Contractor is professionally qualified to provid e such Services and is willing to provide
them to the District on thB terms and conditions set forth herein; and

WHEREAS, this Agreement is not E:?nforceable until s·uch time as the District's Board of Directors
has approved it in a public hearing;

NOW, TH{REFORE, the Parties agree as follow;

1.      HEADINGS
        Headings herein are for convenience of reference only and shall in no way affect
        interpretation of the Agreement.

2.      EXHIBITS
        Exhibits A "Scope of Services" and Exhibit B "Payment Terms" are attached hereto and
        incorporated by reference.

3.      SCOPE OF SERVICES
        Contractor agrees to perform all services described in Exhibit A, for paym ent pursuant to
        Exhibit B, and in accordance with the terms and conditions of this Agreement and those
        described in the District's RFP 24-07 Advan ced Life Support Ambulance Services,
        incorporated herein by reference.




                                                                                        Page 1 of 23

                                                                                                       P69
      These documents, along with the Contractor's response to RFP 24-07, the entirety of this
      Agreement, and any other records or documents furnished by the District during the term
      of this Agreement shall constitute the Contract Documents.

4.    TERM
      This Agreement shall commence on the Effective Date and shall continue in full force and
      in effect for three (3) years. The Agreement may be extended, subject to the written
      agreement from the Parties, for up to two (2) additional twelve (12) month periods

                                                 EXHIBIT A
                                             Scope of Services

The scope of services to be provided by the Contractor shall include the following activities as
needed to meet the District's goals.

1.      Introduction to Scope of Work
As a contracted ambulance provider for Metro Fire, the Contractor will be responsible for delivering
timely, proficient, and compassionate service based on the following goals:

    1. Optimal Patient Care - High-quality advanced prehospital medical care and interventions to
       ensure appropriate level of care and sea mless transition from the prehospital environment to
       more definitive ca re settings, if needed.

    2. Resource Utilization and Adaptability - Int egration of resources into Metro Fire's EMS
       deployment model to ensure maximum effectiven
                                            I
                                                     ess and system-wide
                                                                     •
                                                                         efficiency.

    3.   System Adaptability - Capacity and flexibility for adapting· to deployment changes necessary to
         meet system demand and maintain level of service.

    4.   Fiscal Responsibility - Fair and reasonable fee proposa l that supports service level requirements
         and demonstrates value to the local ratepayer.

2.       Scope of Work Overview
For the purposes of this Agreement, the services requested are generally· classified as follows:

    1. ALS Ambulance S~rvices {Contracted Units) - Contractor shall provide a minimum of ten (10) 12-
       hour ALS units, seven days per week (minimum of 43,800 unit hours per year). Unit hours include
       t ~n (10) minutes at the beginning of a Contracted Unit's shift and fifteen (15) minutes at t he end
       0f a Contracted Unit's shift to complete customar·y beginning and end of shift procedures, e.g.,
       safety and vehicle checks, supply inventory, paperwork completion, etc. Contracted units shall be
       ambulances dedicated to the 9~1-1 system and staffed w ith one Paramedic and one EMT OR two
       Paramedics, and are subject to all re quirements set forth herein.

    2.   ALS Surge Protection (Surge Units) - Contractor sha ll guarantee their capacity to provide up to
         five (5) additional t emporary units to surge into the 9-1-1 system, at the District's request, during
         times of an acute increa·se in patient volume that has the potential to severely challenge or exceed
         the capacity of the loca l EMS System. Requests for additional Surge Units beyond the first five
         units will be based upon the Contractor's availability and the circumsta nces for the request. Surge
         units may also be requested for temporary assignment to maintain service delivery during times
         of ambulance drawdown resulting in a reduction of available resources.

Contractor shall maintain ALS service provider designation with SCEMSA at all times for t he duration of
the Agreement and shall provide proof to the District t hat their ALS service provider designat ion is current
on an annual basis. All licenses and certificat ions shall remain current and in effect for the duration of the
Agreement, inclusive of any Agreement extensions. Licenses and certifications shall be ava ilable for



                                                                                                Page 14 of 23
                                                                                                                  P82
inspection by the District upon request. Contractor and any of the Contractor's personnel providing
services cannot be on the Office of Inspector General (OIG) List of excluded Individuals/Entities (LEIE).

In an effort to ensure maximum operational flexibility, contracted unit posting location and shift times are
subject to change with thirty (30) days prior written notice to the Contractor. It is the intent of the District
to review unit location and shift times for contracted units on a quarterly basis, and make adjustments as
needed to meet operational needs, while maintaining the annual minimum described above. Additionally,
the District intends to review the number of contracted units on an annual basis, and may request
additional contracted units in order to meet operational needs.

For any services provided by t he Contractor on behalf of the District, including surge units as defined
above, the District shall be responsible for billing t he patient or any third-party payor for the services
provided by the Contractor. The Contractor shall not seek payment from the patient or any third-party
payor for any services. The District shall reimburse the C6ntractor at the rates set forth in the contract,
and the Contractor shall accept the rate as payment in full for services. SRFECC shall provide dispatching
services for the Contract or's units at Metro Fire cost.

3.      Requirements
Contractor shall meet or exceed the following requirements outlined below in their performance of the
Scope of Work.

Unless otherwise indicated, all expenses necessary to meet contract requirements and/or perform the
Scope of Work outlined herein will be the sole responsibility of the Contractor.

    1. Ambulance Req1.iirements
       a. Vehicles
             i. All contracted units, including surge units, shall be equipped with all items required by
                the most current version of the ~CEMSA program document, 2030: Advanced Life
                Support Inventories.
            ii. All contracted units, including surge units, shall be equipped with cardiac monitors that
                are capc!ble of performing a 12-lead electrocardiogram (EKG) and transmitting any ST-
                Elevation Myocardial Infarction (+ STEM!) EKGs to the STEMI receiving facility.
           iii. All contracted units, including the first five Surge Units, shall be equipped with a
                mechanical chest compression device that provides consistent compressions t o
                patients i'n cardiac arrest, such as a Lucas Device.
           iv. All contracted units, including the first five Surge Units, shall permanently display the
                name of the Contractor or possess other suitable identification or logo on the outside
                of the vehicle in compliance with State and local statutory or regulatory requirements.
                Any restriping/lettering as a result of this contract shall be at the Contractor's expense.
                Logo shall be approved in writing by Metro Fire prior to insta llation.
            v. All contracted units, including surge units, shall be in good operational and mechanical
                condition, without visible physical damage. Additionally, all ambulances shall meet or
                exceed the requirements of the Ca lifornia Highway Patrol, the California Department of
                Motor Vehicles (DMV), the United States Department of Transportation, and SCEMSA.
           vi. The Contractor shall be responsible for all costs for all routine preventative
                maintenance and repairs of ambulances. Contractor shall adhere to its maintenance
                and maintenance records plan during the contract period. Disruption in service due to
                the Contractor's non-compliance with the plan will be considered a major breach and

                                                                                                 Page 15 of 23
                                                                                                                   P83
            grounds for immediate contract termination.
      vii. When an ambulance is taken out of service due to mechanica l failure or damage, a
            replacement ambulance shall be available in the system within sixty (60) minutes.
     viii. When an ambulance is to be taken out of service for preventative maintenance, a
            replacement ambulance shall be immediately put in place without interruption of
            services under this contract.
b.   Communications
         i. All contracted units, including surge units, shall be equipped w ith a minimum of one
            800 MHz Mobile Radio. This radio shall be P25 compliant and capable of transmitting
            on Sacramento County's Motorola Land Mobile Radio (LMR) system. Radios sha ll be
            programmed with t he fire zones used by t he SRFECC. Setup and programming of the
            radio(s) is the responsibility of the Contractor.
        ii. All contracted units, including surge units, shall be equipped with a minimum of one
            800M Hz Portable Radio per crew m_~mber. The radios shall be P25 compliant and
            capable of transmitting on Sacramenfo County's Motorola LMR system. Radios shall be
            programmed with the fire zones used by the SRFECC. Setup and programming of the
            rad io(s) is the responsibility of t he Contractor.
       iii. All contracted units, including surge units, sha U_be equipped w it h a minim um of one
            Very High Frequency (VHF) radio . The radio shall have the most current programm ing
            used by the Sacram~rito Regional Fire Agencies. Setup and programming of the radio(s)
            are the responsibility of t he Contractor.
       iv. All contracted units, including surge units, shall be equipped with a mobile internet
            router that is active with a cellular provider. Mobile routers sha ll have a Global
            Positioning System (GPS) antenna and the ability to add a GPS server for Automatic
            Vehicle Locator (AVL) information.
        v. All dontracted units, including surge units, shall be equipped with a computer capable
            of running Window_s 7 or Windows 10. Each computer shall have a minimum of 4 GB of
            RAM and a 500 GB SD hard drive in order to install the CAD mobile client. Mobile
            software, such as NetMotion, is required to communicate with SRFECC, CAD, and Metro
            Fire units. Software licensing to connect to CAD shall be obtained directly from SRFECC.
            Approximate cost of a NetMotion license is $135 per unit, per year. Approximate cost
            of the CAD mobile client license is $400 per device, per year. Fees are subject to change
            and are the sole responsibility of the Contractor.
       vi. All contracted units, including surge units, shall have a smart device (i.e. smartphone,
            clean) capable of downloading and operat ing the Tablet Command application. The
            Contractor shall utilize Tablet Command for integration into the District's Command
            and C:ontrol Accountability System. If "Tablet Pro" becomes the required Tablet
            Command application, the Contractor shall be solely responsible for obtaining the
            requ ired license and any cost associated with broadcasting each ambulance Automated
            Video Locator (AVL) locations (cradle point type device) or cellular operations. The
            current cost for "Tablet Pro" licensure is $700 per licensure, per year.
      vii. The Contractor shall be set up as a secondary user under Met ro Fire on the Sacramento
            Regional Radio Communications System (SRRCS) for all 800 MHz radios. There w ill be a
            radio subscription fee of approximately $445 per radio, per year (All secondary user
            subscription fees will be the responsibility of the Contractor. Metro Fire will invoice the
            Contractor for all subscription fees. Invoices are subject to a 15% administration fee.
            Radio subscription fees are subj ect to change based on SRRCS fees assessed to prima ry
            users).

                                                                                        Page 16 of 23

                                                                                                          P84
         viii. In order to maintain interoperability with Metro Fire, receiving hospitals, and SRFECC,
               the Contractor shall be solely responsible for all installation, maintenance, repair, and
               other related costs necessary to ensure that the communication systems described
               herein remain operational at all times.

2. Staffing Requ irements
   a. Personnel
           i. Unit staffing for all contracted units, including surge units, sha ll include a min imum of
              one Sacramento County accredited Paramedic, with the balance of staffing to be filled
              by either one EMT or another Paramedic. Assigned personnel shall be physically capable
              of performing t he services required by t his Agreement. Assigned personnel shall be
              prepared to interface seamlessly with SRFECC and Metro Fire personnel.
          ii. All personnel providing services pursuant to this Agreement shall be tra ined and
              certified as being National Incident Management System (NIMS) compliant at the basic
              level (N IMS 700 & ICS 100 certification).
         iii. Contractor shall use all reasonabie efforts to employ Parc1medics, EMTs, and other
              personnel that possess experience, knowledge, and history of EMS services in
              Sacramento County, including SCEMSA protocols.
         iv. The District's EMS system requires professional and courteous conduct at all times from
              Contractor's field P\;!rsonnel, middle management, and top executives. All personnel
              providing services pursuant to this Agreement shall adhere to all relevant District
              personnel policies/procedures regarding appearance and conduct; provided that such
              personnel policies/procedures are in accordance with applicable laws, Contractor's
              collective bargaining agreement, and Contractor's policies/procedures. The District will
              provide the Cont ractor with copies of its relevant personnel policies/procedures before
              commencement of the Contract period to give Contractor adequate time for the
              selection, assignm~nt, and preparation of assigned employees. Contractor sha ll provide
              t he District with copies of all of its relevant personnel policies/procedures before
              commencement of t he· Contractor period and identify any policies/procedures
              inconsistent with the District's.
          v. All personnel providing services pursuant to this Agreement shall pass a criminal
              background check. The District will not be responsible for any expenses associated with
              the background checks. Background checks sha ll include, but are not limited to, the
              following:
                         A. criminal search (7 years or up to 5 criminal searches),
                         B. sex offender registry check
                         C. Department of Motor Vehicle driving history check, review of OIG list of
                             excluded individuals/entities
                         D. state and local licensure/accreditation verification (Contractor sha ll not
                             assign any personnel to provide services to the District whose
                             EMT/Paramedic        licenses/certifications/accreditations      have     any
                             Disciplinary Orders or Conditions of Probation imposed by the State EMS
                             Authority or SCEMSA.
         vi. Contractor's employees shall report for duty well rested, alert and not under the
              influence of any substance, legal or illegal, that may impair their judgement. It is a policy
              of Metro Fire to have a work environment free from the effects of alcohol, illegal drugs,
              and controlled substance abuse. In order to ensure assigned personnel are fit for duty,
              Contractor must have a program in place for drug and alcohol screening of all personnel

                                                                                            Page 17 of 23

                                                                                                              P85
          providing services pursuant to this Agreement. Further, the Contractor shall
          immediately transport any personnel suspected to be using or under the influence of
          drugs or alcohol or other intoxicant to a facility for testing or have an agent of a testing
          facility come to the location of the employee to obtain a necessary sample. Any
          personnel suspected of being under the influence of any drug or intoxicating substance
          will be immediately relieved of duty by Contractor until there is clinical proof to the
          contrary.
    vii. Contractor personnel that appear on the OIG exclusion list shall not provide services for
          the District nor be assigned to this Agreement.
   viii. Contractor shall ensure that EMTs and paramedics maintain a level of physical fitness
          that allows them to continuously meet the dema'nds of the job.
     ix. Contractor shall ensure that all employees who staff any ambulance as a part of the
1         services are thoroughly familiar with all aspects of vehicle operation and the location
          and use of all on-board equipment and supplies.

          professional uniforms issued by the Contractor.
      ii. Contractor shall ensure that personnel providing services pursuant to this Agreement
          have the appropriate PPE that meet national safety standards for EMS personnel to
          include, but not limi,tEfd to, reflective vest, eye protection, and ear/hearing protection.
     iii. Contractor or their employees shall bear all uniform and PPE related costs including

c. Continuing Education
       i. Training and educational requirements change from time-to-time for Paramedics and

      ii. Contractor shall ensure that relevant and frequent education and training courses are
          offered to assist personnel providing services pursuant to this Agreement maintain

     iii. The Contractor shali require all ambulance personnel in its employment to successfully

          ambulances are operated in a legal and safe manner. The driver training program shall
          be designed (o verify driving proficiency upon hire and updated training shall be
          provided. The driver program shall meet or exceed industry standa rds. The Contractor
          shall ensure that its vehicles are at all times operated in a safe manner.
d. Monitoring and Oversight
       i. Contractor shall utilize reasonable work schedules and shift assignments that allow
          personnel providing services pursuant to this Agreement to work at their optimum level
          of efficiency and provide reasonable rest periods. The Contractor shall provide working
          conditions that assist in attracting and retaining highly qualified personnel.
      ii. Contractor shall utilize management practices that ensure that personnel providing
          services pursuant to this Agreement who are working extended shifts, part-time jobs,
          voluntary overtime, or mandatory overtime are not fatigued to an extent that might
          impair judgment or motor skills.

3.   Performance Requirements
     a.   General Performance
             i. Provision of services pursuant to th.is Agreement requires the highest levels of
                perforfnance and reliability. Contractor shail perform all services pursuant to this
                Agreement in accordance with botn the letter and spirit of all requirements, conditions,
                specifications, expectations, and other parameters delineated in this Agreement, to the
                complete satisfaction of Metro Fire.
           'ii. All statements made and actions taken by the Contractor in the performance of its
                contractual obligations shall be done in a prudent, professional, and courteous manner
                that supports and/or advances Metro Fire's EMS mission of optimizing patient outcome
                by providing superior quality patient care with proficiency and compassion. Most
                importantly, the Contractor decision making and conduct shall always be guided by, and
                reflect, only the highest ethical standards and demonstrate respect and dignity for all
                human beings.
           iii. Clinical and response time performance must be extremely reliable, with equipment
                failure and human error held to an absolute minimum through constant attention to
                performance, protocol, procedure, performance auditing, and prompt definitive
                corrective action as needed.
           iv. Mere demonstration of effort, even diligent and well-intentioned effort, shall not
                substitute for performance results. Performance will be monitored by Metro Fire
                pursuant to the requirements, terms, and conditions of this Agreement.
     b.   Account Management
             i. The Contractor shall designate a dedicated, competent account manager who shall be
                responsible for the Metro Fire account/contract. The account manager shall be the
                primary contact for all issues regarding the Contractor's performance of services
                pursuant to this Agreement. The account manager's office shall be in the Sacramento
                Region. In order to foster teamwork and efficiency, it is imperative that there be an

                                                                                          Page 19 of 23

                                                                                                           P87
          outstanding working relationship and excellent communication between agencies and
          agency liaisons.
c. Capacity and Adaptability
      i. Contractor shall mai~tain staffing levels sufficient to meet its obligations in
          performance of the services provided pursuant to this Agreement.
     ii. All contracted units shall be available for response to a dispatch at the scheduled shift
          start time. Posting location and shift times for contracted units will be determined at
          the Metro Fire's sole discretion. Metro Fire intends to review posting location and shift
          times for contracted units on a quarterly basis, and make adjustments as needed to
          meet operational needs, while maintaining annual minimum obligations.
    iii. Metro Fire intends to review the number of e<;>ntracted units on an annual basis, and
          may request additional contracted units in dder to meet operational needs; District
          shall provide Contractor with a minimum of thirty (30) days written notice of any
          additional contracted units. Contractor's capacity shall be sufficient to be responsive to
          the District's operational needs.

      i. In performance of its obligatiori's pursuant to this Agreement, the Contractor shall abide
          by all applicable Federal, State, and local laws and regulations, including, but not limited
          to:

       i. The Contracto°l" shall ensure that clinical performance, including patient transport, is

                                          Payment Terms

The fee for services shal l not exceed the rates outlined in the Contractor's Hourly Rates Schedule.
Payment for additional services outside the scope of this Agreement may be requested and
approved by the District through an amendment to this Agreement and shall be subject to the
rates outlined in the Contractor's Hourly Rates Schedule.

The Contractor shall submit properly certified invoices to the District. Invoices shall be sent
monthly and shall include the number of unit hours provide□ that month and the unit hour rate.

Invoices shall be sent to:

       ap@metrofire.ca.gov

If invoices cannot be sent via email, invoices shall be mailed to:

       Sacramento Metropolitan FiJe District
       Attn: Finance Division
       10545 Armstrong Ave., Suite 200
       Mather, CA 95655

Fai lure to com ply '-"{ith these requ irements or t d provide an invoice in conformance with this
Agreement document may delay payment.

The Distr!ct will not be bound by prices conta ined in an invoice that are higher than the pricing
contained on the origina l Hourly Rates Schedule. If a price increase has not been accepted in
writing by the District, the invoice may be rejected .

No advance payment shall be made for goods or services furnished by the Contractor pursuant
to this Agreement. Payment terms are net 45 days from the date of receipt of an invoice.

The Contractor's fee shall indlude all costs necessary to provide the required services. The
Contractor's fee shall in~lude, but is not limited to, al l taxes (excluding sales and use tax},
equipment, supplies, staff, and all other charges, including travel expenses, necessa ry to meet
the requirements of this Agreement. The Contractor's fee shall be in the form of the Contractor's
total cost per unit hour ("Unit Hourly Cost" ). For the purposes of the Agreement, a unit hour is
defined as an equipped and staffed ambulance on a respo nse or waiting for a response for one
hour. The Unit Hourly Cost shall include the total cost of providing all services included in Exhibit
A and the RFP response by the Contractor. Unit hours include ten (10) minutes at the beginning
of a Contracted Unit's shift and fifteen (15) minutes at the end of a Contracted Unit's shift to
co mplete customary beginning and end of shift procedures, e.g., safety and vehicle checks,


                                                                                       Page 22 of 23

                                                                                                        P90
su pply inventory, paperwork completion, et c. No additional costs or fees will be considered for
paym ent. Only Unit Hourly Cost w ill be considered for payment. The cost quoted shall be th e cost
M etro Fire will pay for the term of t his Agreement.

Metropolitan Fire District is now utilizing an e-Procurement Porta l (OpenGov).

deadline dates and times. Without exception, responses will not be accepted after
the submission deadline regardl ess of any technical difficulties such as poor
internet connections. The District strongly recommends completing your response
well ahead of the deadline.

                  1.0      RESTRICTION ON COMMUNICATION WITH STAFF
                  Unless otherwise instructed in this RFP, once this RFP is issued, and until the selection of a Contractor has
                  been made and announced, all communication shall be submitted through OpenGov. Under no
                  circumstance will verbal answers or comments be binding. The District will assume no responsibility for
                  oral instructions or suggestions. Only direct communication documented through OpenGov will be
                  considered valid in this process. The District reserves the right to reject any submission for violation of
                  this provision. Contractors shall submit all questions regarding this RFP through OpenGov:
                  https://secure.OpenGov.com/portal/metrofire. Should the Contractor find discrepancies in, or omissions
                  from the scope, or shou ld the Contractor be in doubt as to their meaning in the RFP, the Contractor must
                  notify the District in writing via OpenGov prior to the Question Submission Deadline identified in Section
                  3.0. All answers to questions will be posted on OpenGov. Contractors may also click on this RFP in
                  OpenGov ·and click "Follow" to receive an email notification when answers are posted. It is the
                  responsibility of the Contractor to check the website for answers to questions.

                  2.0              AMENDMENTS/ADDENDA
                  The District reserves the right tci issue amendments and addenda to this RFP. Contractors are required to
                  register for an account through OpenGov. Once the Contractor has completed th eir registration, in order
                  for the Contractor to receive amendment/addenda notifications via email, the Contractor must click on
                  this RFP and click on "Follow." It is the Contractor's responsibility to obtain any and all amendments and
                  addenda and to submit the document(s) required in advance of the submission deadline. A proposal may
                  be deemed non responsive for failing to submit the latest version of the RFP.

                  3.0              RFP SCHEDULE

                  The District reserves the right to modify the RFP schedule.

                  4.0              SUBMISSION OF QUESTIONS
                  Prior to submitting a proposal, Contractors shall thoroughly examine the RFP and its attachments in order
                  t o understand the scope of work for the services. Any questions, concerns, errors, or ambiguities noted
                  by the Contractor during said examination shall immediately be called to th e attention of the District and
                  submitted through OpenGov prior to the Question Submission Deadline identified in Section 3.0.

                  5.0              INTRODUCTION
                  The Sacramento Metropolitan Fire District (hereinafter referred to as Metro Fire or the District) is soliciting
                  proposals from qualified firms (Contractor) to provide 9-1-1 Advanced Life Support (ALS) ambulance
                  services as a supplemental service to Metro Fire's current ambulance and Emergency Medical Services
                  (EMS). The awarded Contractor, shall provide the requested services in accordance with the requirements
                  specified in this RFP. All ambulance services described in this RFP document refer only to ground
                  ambulance services. The District does not guarantee that the Contractor will be assigned any particular
                  number of dispatch requ ests. Prior to submitting a proposal, Contractors are advised to carefully read this
                  RFP in its entirety.
