                 6.0      BACl<GROUND
                 Metro Fire is a Special District of the County of Sacramento, operating under an elected Board of Directors.
                 In 2000, Metro Fire was formed through a Local Agency Formation Commission (LAFCO) approved
                 process, merging 16 smaller fire departments. As the seventh largest fire district in the State of California,
                 Metro Fire serves a population of over 720,000 and has a land area of 359 square miles. It is located in
                 Sacramento County, California and provides services to the Cities of Rancho Cordova and Citrus Heights,
                 in addition to unincorporated areas of the County and a small area of Placer County. The services provided
                 by the District include: fire protection, building safety regulation and inspection, hazardous materials,
                 technical rescue, arson investigation, and emergency medical response and transport.

                 Metro Fire is dispatched by the Sacramento Regional Fire/EMS Communications Center (SRFECC) located
                 in Sacramento, California. SRFECC is funded through a Joint Powers Authority (JPA) of participating fire
                 agencies within the County and has one of the highest call volumes of all dispatch centers in the United
                 States, answering nearly 500,000 calls per year. The center utilizes a Northrop/Grumman Computer-Aided
                 Dispatch (CAD) system to initiate response of necessary fire apparatus and ambulances.

                 Metro Fire's EMS Division is responsible for the District's provision of emergency medical response
                 services, including Advanced Life Support (ALS) and Basic Life Support (BLS) pre-hospital medical aid and
                 ground emergency transport, delivered through the strategic deployment of ALS-capable first responder
                 units (engines, trucks and squads) staffed with firefighter-paramedics; dual-role Fire Department Medic
                 (FDM) ambulance units staffed with firefighter-paramedics; single-role Metro Medic Program (MMP)
                 ambulance units staffed with paramedics and Emergency Medical Technicians (EMTs) (non-firefighter);
                 and contracted third-party ALS ambulance units. Additional surge protection is also provided through
                 contracted third-party ALS ambulance units to augment the EMS system during peak periods. One
                 Assistant Chief, five Battalion Chiefs, and one Captain (EMS24) are responsible for daily oversight of EMS
                 field operations.

                 Metro Fire participates in a countywide emergency response system without boundaries, meaning units
                 under a contract with Metro Fire to provide ambulance services may be dispatched to respond anywhere
                 in the County. Medic units transport patients to 11 local hospitals, and on occasion, additional hospitals
                 in surrounding counties. Sutter Health, Dignity Health, Kaiser Permanente, the Veteran's Administration,
                 and the University of California, Davis (UC Davis) are the major hospital groups operating in Sacramento
                 County. Metro Fire is also working w ith Sacrament o County to develop protocols for Transport to
                 Alternative Destinations (TAD) and anticipates implementation of t hose protocols during the intended
                 contract term.

                 7.0     MINIMUM QUALIFICATIONS
                 To be eligible to submit a proposal, Contractors shall meet or exceed the following requirements:

                      1.   Have been regularly and continuously engaged in the business of providing emergency ALS
                           ambulance services operating in a 9-1-1 system for at least three (3) years. Experience operating
                           in a California 9-1-1 system is preferred.

                      2.   Possess all required certifications, insurance, and licenses required to perform the services
                           outlined within this RFP. All licenses and certifications shall be current and in effect at the time of
                           proposal submission and shall remain current and in effect for the duration of any subsequent
                           contract, inclusive of any contract extensions. Licenses and certifications shall be available for
                           inspection by the District upon request.

      3.   All of the Contractor's existing contracts shall be in good standing with no delinquent obligations,

      4.   Currently utilize a National EMS Information System (NEMSIS) version 3.5 (or greater) compliant
           Electronic Patient Care Reporting (ePCR) system. Compliant means a system that has been tested
           and certified by NEMSIS. System must have the capability to share all reporting data with Metro
           Fire. Metro Fire presently uses ImageTrend as its ePCRsolution. To support operational efficiency,
           continuum of care, and data accuracy, the use of ImageTrend by the selected Contractor will be
           required for this contract. Contractors presently using other NEMSIS version 3.5 (or greater)
           compliant ePCR systems are still eligible to submit a proposal.

           the requirements of Sacramento County Emergency Medical Services Agency (SCEMSA) program
           documents 7600: Quality Improvement Program and 7602: Quality Assurance Program for ALS
           providers.

           transmitting any ST-Elevation Myocardial Infarction(+ STEMI) EKGs to the STEMI receiving facility.

      7. Contractor and any of the Contractor's personnel providing services cannot be on the Office of
         Inspector General (OIG) List of Excluded Individuals/Entities (LEIE).

      8.   Utilize a mec~anical chest compression device that provides consistent compressions to patients
           in cardiac arrest, such as a Lucas Device.

8.0        SCOPE OF WORK
8.1      Introduction to Scope of Work
M etro Fire has a rich history of protecting its citizens through a myriad of critical functions, including
emergency medical response services. Metro Fire has continuously adapted to the changing community
and operational needs by utilizing public-private partnerships. Metro Fire maintains complete
administrative and operational control of th e ambulances operating its EMS System according to its
authority and duty under California Government Code, Title 5, Division 2, Part 1, Section 54980 and
California Health and Safety Code Section 1797.201, and a settlement agreement between the County of
Sacramento and the District.

As an EMS provider, Metro Fire serves a critical role in a coordinated system that ensures patients receive
the appropriate level of care at every stage, from the moment a 9-1-1 call is made to the point of definitive
treatment or recovery. This coordinated system, also known as the "continuum of care," encompasses
every phase of patient interaction, including initial emergency response, prehospital care, transport,
hospital admission, and post-discharge follow-up, ensuring that patients experience a consistent and high-
quality care process throughout their journey.

Metro Fire's EMS delivery is a crucial link in this continuum of care by providing rapid response, patient
assessment, on-scene treatment and/or stabilization, transport if necessary to an appropriate facility
based on patient's needs, and follow-up for high-risk patients. The integration of these services into the
broader healthcare system is essential for ensuring overall system efficien cy and supporting the
continuum of care.

              As a contracted ambulance provider for Metro Fire, the Contractor will be responsible for delivering
              timely, proficient, and compassionate service based on the following goals:

                    1. Optimal Patient Care - High-quality advanced prehospital medical care and interventions to
                       ensure appropriate level of care and seamless transition from the prehospital environment to
                       more definitive care settings, if needed.

                   2.    Resource Utilization and Adaptability - Integration of resources into Metro Fire's EMS
                         deployment model to ensure maximum effectiveness and system-wide efficiency.

                   3. System Adaptability - Capacity and flexibility for adapting to deployment changes necessary to
                      meet system demand and maintain level of service.

                    4.   Fiscal Responsibility - Fair and reasonable fee proposal that supports service level requirements
                         and demonstrates value to the local ratepayer.

               8.2 Scope of Work Overview
               For the purposes of this RFP and any contract executed pursuant to it, the services requested are generally
               classified as follows:

                    1. ALS Ambulance Services (Contracted Units) - Contractor shall provide a minimum of ten (10) 12-
                       hour ALS units, seven days per week (minimum of 43,800 unit hours per year). Contracted units
                       shall be ambulances dedicated to the 9-1-1 system and staffed with one Paramedic and one EMT
                       OR two Paramedics, and are subject to all requirements set forth herein.

                    2.   ALS Surge Protection (Surge Units) - Contractor shall guarantee their capacity to provide
                         additional temporary units to surge into the 9-1-1 system, at the District's request, during times
                         of an acute increase in patient volume that has the potential to severely challenge or exceed the
                         capacity of the local EMS System. Surge units may also be requested for temporary assignment to
                         maintain service delivery during times of ambulance drawdown resulting in a reduction of
                         available resources.

              The start date for th e requested services shall be July 1, 2025. Contractor shall possess a current written
              ALS service provider designation agreement with SCEMSA prior to July 1, 2025. Contractor shall maintain
              ALS service provider designation with SCEMSA at all times for the duration of the agreement and shall
              provide proof to the District that their ALS service provider designation is current on an annual basis.

              In an effort to ensure maximum operat ional flexibility, contracted unit posting location and shift times are
              subject to change. It is the intent of the District to review unit location and shift times for contracted units
              on a quarterly basis, and make adjustments as needed to meet operational needs, w hile maintaining the
              annual minimum described above. Additionally, the District intends to review the number of contra cted
              units on an annual basis, and may request additional contracted units in order to meet operational needs.
              Contractor's proposal shall demonstrate capacity and adaptability to be responsive t o the District's
              operational needs.

              For any services provided by the Contractor on behalf of the District, including surge units as defined
              above, the District shall be responsible for billing the patient or any third-party payor for the services
              provided by the Contractor. The Contractor shall not seek payment from the patient or any third-party
              payor for any services. The Dist rict shall reimburse the Contractor at the rates set forth in the contract,

 8.3 Requirements
 In addition to the minimum qualifications outlined in Section 7.0, Contractor shall meet or exceed the
 following requirements outlined below in their performance of the Scope of Work.

 Unless otherwise indicated, all expenses necessary to meet RFP/contract requirements and/or perform
 the Scope of Work outlined in this RFP will be the sole responsibility of the Contractor.

        1. Ambulance Requirements
                      a. Vehicles
                             i. All contracted units, including surge units, shall be equipped with all items required by
                                the most current version of the SCEMSA program document, 2030: Advanced Life
                                Support Inventories.
                            ii. All contracted units, including surge units, shall be equipped with cardiac monitors that
                                are capable of performing a 12-lead electrocardiogram (EKG) and t ransmitting any ST-
                                Elevation Myocardial Infarction(+ STEM!) EKGs t o the STEM ! receiving facility.
                           iii. All contracted units, including surge units, shall be equipped with a mechanical chest
                                compression device that provides consistent compressions to patients in cardiac arrest,
                                such as a Lucas Device.
                           iv. All contracted units, including surge ·units, shall permanently display the name of the
                                Contractor or possess other suitable identification or logo on the outside of the vehicle
                                in compliance with State and local statutory or regulatory requirements. Any
                                restriping/lettering as a result of this contract shall be at the Contractor's expense. Logo
                                shall be approved in writ ing by Metro Fire prior to installation.
                            v. All contracted units, including surge units, shall be in good operational and mechanical
                                condition, without visible physical damage. Additiona lly, all ambulances sha ll meet or
                                exceed the requirements of the California Highway Patrol, the Californ ia Department of
                                Motor Vehicles (DMV), the United States Department ofTransportation, and SCEMSA.
                            vi. The Contractor shall be responsible for all costs for all routine preventative
                                maintenance and repairs of ambulances. Contractor shall adhere to its maintenance
                                and maintenance records plan during the contract period. Disruption in service due to
                                the Contractor's non-compliance with t he plan will be considered a major breach and
                                grounds for immediate contract termination.
                           vii. When an ambulance is t aken out of service due t o mechanical fai lure or damage, a
                                replacement ambulance shall be available in the system within sixty (60) m inutes.
                          viii. When an ambulance is to be taken out of service for preventative maintenance, a
                                replacement ambulance shall be immediately put in place without interruption of
                                services under this contract.
                      b. Communications
                             i. All contracted units, including surge units, shall be equipped with a minimum of one
                                800 MHz Mobile Radio. This radio shall be P25 compliant and capable of transmitting
                                on Sacram ento County's Motorola Land Mobile Radio (LMR) systei:n. Radios shall be
                                programmed with the fire zones used by the SRFECC. Setup and programming of the
                                radio(s) is the responsibility of the Contractor.
                            ii. All contracted units, including surge units, shall be equipped with a minimum of one
                                800MHz Portable Radio per crew member. The radios shall be P25 compliant and
                                capable of transmitting on Sacramento Cou nty's Motorola LMR system. Radios shall be

    3.   Performance Requirements
         a. General Performance
                i. Provision of services pursuant to this RFP and any resulting contract requires the highest
                    levels of performance and reliability. Contracto r shall perform all services pursuant to
                    this RFP and any resulting contract in accordance with both the letter and spirit of all
                    requirements, conditions, specifications, expectations, and other parameters
                    delineated in this RFP and any resulting contract, to the complete satisfaction of Metro
                    Fi re.
               ii. All statements made and actions taken by the Contractor in the performance of its
                    contractual obligations shall be done in a prudent, professional, and courteous manner
                    that supports and/or advances Metro Fire's EMS mission of optimizing patient outcome
                    by providing superior quality patient care with proficiency and compassion. Most
                    importantly, the Contractor decision making and conduct shall always be guided by, and
                    reflect, only the highest ethical standards and demonstrate. respect and dignity for all
                    human beings.
              iii. Clinical and response time performance must be extremely reliable, with equipment
                    failure and human error held to an absolute minimum through constant attention to
                    performance, protocol, procedure, perform ance auditing, and prompt definitive
                    corrective action as needed.
              iv. Mere demonstration of effort, even diligent and well-intentioned effort, shall not
                    substitute for performance results. Performance will be monitored by Metro Fire
                    pursuant to the requirements, terms, and conditions of this RFP and any resulting
                    contract.
         b. Account M anagement
                i. The Contractor sha ll designate a dedicated, competent account manager who shall be
                    responsible for the Metro Fire account/contract. The account manager shall be the
                    primary cont act for all issues regarding t he Contractor's performance of services
                    pursuant to t his RFP and any resulting contract. The account manager's office shall be
                    in the Sacramento Region. In order t o foster teamwork and efficiency, it is imperative
                    that there be an outstanding working relationship and excellent communication
                    between agencies and agency liaisons.
         c. Capacity and Adaptability
                 i. Contractor shall maint ain staffing levels sufficient t o meet its obligations in
                    performance of the services provided pursuant to th is RFP and any resulting contract.
               ii. All contracted units shall be available for response to a dispatch at the scheduled shift
                    start time. Posting location and shift times for contracted units will be determined at
                    the Metro Fire's sole discretion. Metro Fire intends to review posting location and shift
                    times for contracted units on a quarterly basis, and make adjustments as needed to
                    meet operational needs, while maintaining annual minimum obligations.
              iii. Metro Fire intends to review the number of contracted units on an annual basis, and
                    may request additional cont racted units in order to meet operational needs.
                    Cont ractor's capacity shall be sufficient to be responsive to t he Dist rict's operational
                    needs.
         d. Legal Compliance
                i. In performance of its obligations pursuant to this RFP and any resulting contract, the

                                               Contractor shall abide by all applicable Federal, State, and local laws and regulations,
                                               including, but not limited to:
                                                    1) Departm ent of Industrial Relations (DIR), Division of Workers' Compensation
                                                        (DWC), and Office of Self-Insurance Plans (OSIP)
                                                    2) Cal OSHA Requirements
                                                   3) State and Federal Employment Law
                                                   4) Harassment and Discrimination Law
                                                    5) Health Insurance Portability & Accountability Act (HIPAA)
                                                    6) Medicare/Medicaid Reporting
                                                    7) California Health & Safety Code, Division 2.5
                                                    8) California Code of Regulations, Title 22, Division 9, Chapter 2
                                                    9) California Vehicle Code
                                                    10) Sacram ento County EMS Agency EMS Agency Policies and Protocols
                                           ii. The Contractor shall ensure that all personnel providing services pursuant to this RFP
                                               and any resulting contract have sufficient understanding of, and at all times are in
                                               compliance with, all applicable federal, state and local EMS-related laws including, but
                                               not limited to: the California Health & Safety Code, Division 2.5, the California Code of
                                               Regulations, Title 22, Division 9, Chapter 2, and the California Vehicle Code.
                                    e.   Protocol Compliance
                                            i. The Contractor shall ensure that clinical performance, including patient transport, is
                                               consistent with and complies with all medical standards, protocols, and guidelines set
                                               forth by the State and SCEMSA; Metro Fire's policies and procedures; as well as the
                                               Contractor's internal protocols. The Contractor, including any individual providing
                                               services pursuant to this RFP and any resulting contract, shall immediately bring to the
                                               attention of Metro Fire EMS Battalion Chief/CQI Manager any protocol that appears to
                                               conflict with other protocols in order to reconcile the inconsistency, contradiction,
                                               and/or ambiguity.
                                           ii. Metro Fire is currently eligible to participate in the Transport to Alternation
                                               Destinations (TAD) and anticipates expanding its TAD participation in accordance with
                                               standards, protocols, and guidelines set forth by the State and SCEMSA. The Contractor
                                               shall comply and participate in future deployment and use of TAD at the direction of
                                               Metro Fire. Costs associated with TAD training and certification requirements outlined
                                               by SCEMSA shall be borne solely by the Contractor.
                                    f.   Non-Discrimination
                                            i. The Contractor shall provide all services pursuant to this RFP and any resulting contract
                                               without regard to the patient's national origin, ethnicity, color, religion, sexual
                                               orientation, gender, age, insurance status, ability/inability to pay, or any other
                                               classification protected by federal or California State Constitutional or statutory law.
                                               Any violation of this policy will be deemed a major breach and grounds for immediate
                                               contract termination.
                                    g.   Quality Improvement and Assurance
                                            i. The Contractor shall maintain a comprehensive QIP and QAP system that meets the
                                               requirements specified in SCEMSA program documents 7600 Quality Improvement
                                               Program and 7602 Quality Assurance Program.
                                           ii. The Contractor shall maintain a customer service outreach program that includes
                                               customer satisfaction surveys for services provided pursuant to this RFP and any
                                               resulting contract. The Contractor shall notify the Metro Fire EMS Assistant Chief and
                                               CQI Manager in writing of all complaints and the resolution outcome.

                i. Contractor shall utilize lmageTrend ePCR software that is compliant with NEMSIS

                   provision of services pursuant to this RFP and any resulting contract.

                   to enhance service delivery.

9.0     CONTRACT TERM
Contract shall be in effect for three (3) years from the contract effective date. The contract may be
extended, subject to written notice of agreement from the District and the Contractor, for up to two (2)
additional twelve (12) month periods beyond the primary contract period. Said extensions shall be subject
to the same terms and conditions as the present contract.

10.0     PROPOSAL REQUIREMENTS
To be considered responsive, Contractors shall submit a written response that clearly demonstrates their
qualifications, experience, and ability to successfully provide the Services stated herein. The proposal shall
reflect a complete and detailed approach to completing the Services and be prepared in a clear and
concise manner, in the outlined format below, using "layman" explanations for technical terminology.
Proposals shall be no more than 40 45 typed pages, using 12-point font size, excluding the following
requested attachments:
     1. Copy of licenses
     2. Organizational chart
    3. List of office locations
    4. Resumes and certificates for key personnel
    5. Copy of QAP/QIP
     6. Copy of Contractor's policies related to ethical standards, managerial philosophy, customer
         services standards, employee education and training, background checks, vehicle maintenance,
         confidentiality, HIPPAA, and data security
    7. /1.udited Financial statements
    8. Listing of litigation and investigations
    9. Copy of agreement or contracts currently in effect with personnel or labor groups that may have
         an impact during the period of the contract
     10. Signature page of RFP
     11. Non-Collusion Declaration Form
     12. Workers' Compensation Declaration Form
     13. Fee Proposal Form
     14. Table of Contents & Tabs/Section Dividers

Additional attachments/exhibits will not be considered during the evaluation process.

Although many items in this RFP document will have express language such as "proposals sha ll include ...,"
Contractors should not infer that because such similar language is absent regarding other items that they
can omit explanations of how they would satisfy the letter or intent of those items.

purchasing@metrofire.ca.gov.

deemed nonresponsive.

11.0        COSTS OF PROPOSAL PREPARATION
The Contractor assumes all costs associated with the preparation and submission of the RFP submittal.
The District will not pay any costs associated with the preparation, submittal, interview, or presentation
of any kind.

12.0        PROPOSAL IRREVOCABLE
A proposal is irrevocable and may not be withdrawn after its opening until it has been considered and
either rejected or accepted by the District, or the RFP has been cancelled. In consideration of th e Dist rict's
reliance on and investigation and consideration of the submitted proposal, the Contractor agrees that
such proposal shall be irrevocable and shall not be w ithdraw n for ninety (90} calendar days following the
proposal opening even though an award may be made to another Contractor. Thereafter, such proposal
shall be automatically relieved.

13.0        EVALUATION
An evaluation committee assembled by the District will review the responses based upon the evaluation
criteria.

14.0        EVALUATION CRITERIA
The evaluation committee will evaluate each proposal to determine its responsiveness to the District's
requirements. Each section of the proposal will be scored in relation to the evaluation committee's
assessment of the demonstrated ability to meet the District's needs, anticipated value brought to the
District, and conformance to submittal requirements.

Evaluation will be based upon the following criteria:

                                                                                 Weight
                                          Criteria

                   Organizational Qualifications and Experience                    15%

                   Patient Care Approach                                            20%

                   Resource Utilization and Adaptability                            20%

                   Syst em Adaptability                                            10%

                   Past Performance                                                 15%

                   Fee Proposal                                                     20%


 The District reserves th e right to request additional information which, in its sole opinion, is necessary to
 assure that the Contractor's competence, staffing, business organization, and financial resources are
 adequate t o perform the required Services for the District.

 Further, the District reserves th e right, at its sole discretion, to requ est clarifications of proposa ls or to
 conduct discussions for the purpose of clarification with any or all Contractors. The purpose of any such
 discussion shall be to ensure full understanding of the proposa l. If clarifications are made as a result of
 such discussion, the Contractor shall put such clarification in writing.

 15.0       RESPONSIBLE CONTRACTOR
 A responsible entity is one that has demonstrated t he attributes of trustworthiness, as well as quality,
 fitness, capacity, and experien ce to satisfactorily perform the scope of work. A Contractor that is

  disqualified.

  Before a contract is awarded, the District may, at its discretion, require from the Contractor furth er
  evidence of qualification, ability to perform, and financial responsibility, and may consider such evidence
  in making the decision on the award of this contract. Notwithstanding the Contractor's affirmation that

   16.0     RESPONSIVE PROPOSAL
   In order to be considered responsive, Contractors must, at a minimum, submit all items listed in Section
   10.0, must be professionally qualified to perform the services required, and must demonstrate sufficient
   experience in performing services of similar size, scope, and complexity.

   17.0     SELECTION PROCESS
       1. An evaluation committee will score all proposals and identify the top-scoring proposal.
       2. The Contractor whose proposal received the top score will be asked t o negotiate a contract that
          will be submitted to the District's Board of Directors for final approval at a publicly noticed
          meeting.
          The District's Purchasing Division will publish a notice of intent to engage in contract negotiations
            ("Notice of Intent") on OpenGov. Within fourteen (14) calendar days fo llowing the issuance of the
            Notice of Intent, the Contractor shall submit to the District:
                a.   Applicable Certificates of Insurance as described in Section 19.0 of this RFP.
                b.   Executed Contract (See Sample Contract attachment)
                c.   County of Sacramento Payee Data Record if not already established with the County
                d.   Proof of current SCEMSA ALS service provider designation, if available. Proof must be
                     received prior to July 1, 2025.
       3. The Board of Directors will have final approval of the contract award.

   18.0     NOTICE OF AWARD
  The District intends to award a contract for the services described in this RFP to the most responsive and
  responsible Contractor who demonstrates the best value for the District. Notification of contract award
  will be made following the evaluation of all proposals and after Board approval.

   Award will be subject to approval by the District's Board of Directors and execution of a written contract,
   approved by the Board of Directors. The District reserves the right to reject any or all proposals offered in
   response to this request and either reissue the RFP or take any other action permitted by statute.

   19.0     INSURANCE REQUIREMENTS
  Upon notification of an intent to award, the prospective Contractor shall furnish Metro Fire with
  certificate(s) evidencing the insurance coverage required below. Copies of required endorsements must
  be attached to the provided certificate. It is the responsibility of the Contractor to notify their insurance
  advisor or insurance carrier(s) regarding coverage, limits, forms and other insurance requirements
  specified below. All documents must be received and approved by Metro Fire before work commences.
  The required insurance coverages shall be consistently maintained for the duration of the contract
  without a lapse in coverage. Please note, the required coverages outlined below shall not limit the amount
  of coverage provided, but shall be the minimum requirements acceptable to the District.

        GENERAL LIABILITY - shall be on an Occurrence basis (as opposed to Claims Made basis).
        Contractor's insurance shall be primary and non-contributory. Minimum limits and structure shall
        be:
            • General Liability Aggregate:                      $3,000,000
            • Products Completed Operations Aggregate:          $3,000,000
            • Personal & Adv Injury:                            $1,000,000
            • Each Occurrence:                                  $1,000,000
            • Fire Damage                                       $100,000

        AUTOMOBILE LIABILITY
           • Commercial Automobile Liability (for Corporate/business owned vehicles including non-
             owned and hired) - $5,000,000 Combined Single Limit.
           • Personal Lines Automobile Liability (for individually owned vehicles, $250,000 per person,
             $500,000 each accident) - $100,000 property damage.

         WORKERS COMPENSATION and EMPLOYER'S LIABILITY
           • The policy shall be endorsed to waive the insurer's subrogation rights against the District.
           • Per statute
           • $1,000,000 per accident for each accident
           • $1,000,000 for disease

         PROFESSIONAL LIABILITY
            •    Professional Liability or Errors and Omissions Liability: $2,000,000 per claim and
                 aggregate.

         PARAMEDIC INCIDENTAL MEDICAL MALPRACTICE
            • $5,000,000 per occurrence and aggregate

         CYBER LIABILITY
            • $10,000,000 per occurrence and aggregate

        ADDITIONAL INSURED
        The Sacramento Metropolitan Fire District, its officers, directors, officials, employees, and
        volunteers are to be endorsed as additional insureds on the Contractor's General Liability and
        Auto policies as respects: liability arising out of activities performed by or on behalf of Cont ractor;
        products and completed operations of Contractor; premises owned, occupied or used by
        Contractor; or automobiles owned, leased, hired or borrowed by Contractor. The coverage shall
        contain no endorsed limitations on the scope of protection afforded to District, its officers,
        directors, officials, employees, or volunteers. A severability of interest provision must apply for
        all the additional insureds, ensuring t hat Contractor's insurance shall apply separately to each
        insured against whom a claim is made or suit is brought, except w ith respect to the insurer's limits
        of liability.

         PRIMARY & NON-CONTRIBUTORY
         Coverage provided by Contractor shall be primary and any insu rance or self-insurance procured
         or maintained by the District shall not be required to contribute w ith it. The limits of insurance
         required herein may be satisfied by a combination of primary and umbrella or excess insurance.

            law or regulation that might affect the rights of th e District under this RFP by signing the Request for
            Proposal. Responses submitted th at do not have all signat ure fields of this RFP signed may not be
            accepted. The Dist rict may contact Contractors to clarify informat ion contained in t heir proposal
            submittal.

            20.02 References to Statutes, Rules of Law, or Regulations
            Any references in t his RFP to any statute, rule of law, or regulati on are deemed to include the most recent
            amendments thereto or replacements thereof. The District may refuse t o award a contract to a Contractor
            who has not complied w ith applicable State and Federal licensing regulations or bylaws or any other
            requirements. Each Cont ractor warrants that th e products and services it will supply to t he Dist rict
            conform in all respects t o the standards set forth by State and Federal licensing regu lations.

            20.03 Conflict of Interest
            By submitting a proposal, t he Contractor represents and w arrants t hat it presently has no interest, and
            shall not obtain any interest, direct or indirect, w hich would conflict in any manner with the performance

               20.04 Gratuities
               No person will offer, give or agree to give any District employee or its representatives any gratuity,
               entertainment, gift, special service, discount, or offer of employment in connection with the award of

               employment in connection with a District contract. Contractor will report any attempt by any employee,
               representative, or consultant of the District to obtain such favors to the Office of the Fire Chief.

               20.05 Anti-Corruption/Anti-Fraud
               Each Party (District and Contractor} agrees not to make, authorize, offer, or promise to make or give any
               money or any other thing of va lue, directly or indirectly, to any current or former government official or
               employee, candidate for political office, or an official of a political party, or any employee, director or
               consultant of a non-government client or potent ial client, for the purpose of securing any improper or
               unfair advantage or obtaining or retaining business in connection with the activities contemplated
               hereunder or for the purpose of improperly inducing or rewarding favorable treatment or advantage in
               connection with this RFP and any resulting contract. Each Party agrees to immediately notify the other of
               any request that it receives to take any action that might constitute, or be construed as, a violation of the
               anti-corruption and anti-bribery laws.

               The Contractor shall desist, and shall ensure that each of its subcontractors and agents desist, from all
               practices that may lead to penal liability due to fraud or embezzlement, bribery, acceptance of bribes, or
               other corruption crimes on the part of persons employed by Contractor or its subcontractors or agents.
               The Contractor warrants that it has not committed any of the aforementioned acts nor has it been the
               subject of any relevant investigation or inqu iry.

               20.06 Required Review and Waiver of Objections by Contractors
               Contractors should carefully review this RFP and any attachments for comments, qu estions, defects,
               objections, or any other matter requiring clarification or correction (collectively called "comments"}.
               Comments concerning RFP objections must be made in writing and received by the District via OpenGov
               no laterthah t he Question Submission Deadline detailed in Section 3.0 of this RFP. This will allow issuance
               of any necessary amendments and help prevent the opening of defective proposals upon which contract
               award could not be made.

               Protests based on any objection w ill be considered waived and invalid if t hese faults have not been
               brought to the attention of the District, in writing, by the Question Submission Deadline.

20.07 Nondiscrimination
No person will be excluded from participation in, be denied benefits of, be discriminated against in the
admission or access to, or be discriminated against in treatment or employment in the District's
contracted programs or activities on the grounds of disability, age, race, color, religion, sex, national
origin, or any other classification protected by federal or California State Constitutional or statutory law;
nor will they be excluded from participation in, be denied benefits of, or be otherwise subjected to
discrimination in the performance of contracts with the District or in the employment practices of the
District's contractors. Accordingly, all Contractors entering into contracts with the District will, upon
request, be required to show proof of such nondiscrimination and to post in conspicuous places, available
to all employees and applicants, notices of nondiscrimination.

 20.08 Proposal Amendment-After Submission and RFP Closing Date
 Proposals submitted may be withdrawn and re-submitted with amendments prior to the RFP Proposal
 Submission Deadline via OpenGov. Proposal amendments submitted in any other manner shall not be
 accepted or considered by the District.

 Contractors are liable for all errors or omissions contained in their proposal submittal. Contractors will
 not be allowed to alter proposal submittals after the Proposal Submission Deadline. Any attempts to
 amend a submitted proposal by way of a letter or facsimile or any other document or means, which would
 result in a proposal being incomplete, ambiguous, inconsistent, or otherwise noncom pliant, shall result in
 the proposal being rejected. The District will not accept any amendments, revisions, or alterations to
 proposals after the Proposal Submission Deadline unless such is formally requested, in writing, by the
  District.

  20.09 Incorrect Proposal Information
  If the District determines that a Contractor has provided, for consideration in the evaluation process or
  contract negotiations, incorrect information which the Contractor knew or should have known was
  materially incorrect, that proposal will be determined non responsive, and the proposal will be rejected.

   20.10 Prohibition of Contractor Terms and Conditions
  A Contractor may not submit the Contractor's own contract terms and conditions in a response to this
  RFP. If a proposal contains such terms and conditions, the District, at its sole discretion, may determine
  the proposal to be a nonresponsive counter-offer, and the proposal may be rejected.

   20.11 Additional Services
   If a Contractor indicates an offer of services in addition to those required by and described in this RFP,
   these additional services may be added to the contract before contract signing at the sole discretion of
   the District. Any additional services proposed will not be considered in the proposal evaluations.

   20.12 Negotiation
   By submitting a proposal, a Contractor accepts that a contract may be concluded upon notification by the
   District and upon Board approval. However, the District reserves the right to negotiate the terms and
   conditions of the contract and the unit hour cost with the highest scoring Contractor. If the parties, after
   having bargained in good faith, are unable to conclude a formal contract within 14 calendar days, the
   District and the Contractor will be released, without penalty, or further obligations other than any
   surviving obligations regarding confidentiality and the District may, at its own discretion, contact other
   Contractors whose proposals are considered suitable for the Services and attempt to conclude a formal
    contract with them.

  20.13 Credit Check
  If requested by the District, the successful Contractor agrees to allow and authorize the District to conduct
  a credit check. A "Credit Application" form shall be completed and returned to the District within 24 hours
  after receipt by the successful Contractor, if so requested by the District.

  20.14 Right of Rejection
  The District reserves the right, at its sole discretion, to reject any and all proposals or to cancel this RFP in
   its entirety.

  Any proposal received which does not meet the requirements of this RFP may be considered to be
  nonresponsive, and the proposal may be rejected. Contractors must comply with all of the terms of this
  RFP and all applicable Federal, State, and local laws and regulations. The District may reje ct any proposal
  that does not comply with all of the terms, conditions, and performance requirements of this RFP. The
  District will reject proposals from any Contractor who does not meet eligibility and licensing requirements
  or for whom there is documented evidence of inability to meet S!:!rvice performance requirements.

   Contractors may not restrict the rights of the District or otherwise qualify their proposals. If a Contractor
   does so, the District may determine the proposal to be a nonresponsive counter-offer, and the proposal
   may be rejected. The District, at its discretion, may reject as incomplete any proposal which is in any way
   conditional, includes exceptions, alterations or omissions, or includes reservations to the t erms of this
   RFP.

   The District reserves the right to reject any proposal based on prior services rendered by the Contractor
   that in the District's opinion have not demonstrated proven satisfactory performance or demonstrated
   satisfactory completion of Services of similar size, scope, and complexity. Whether a service meets this
   requirement shall be at the sole decision of the District.

   The lowest monetary proposal of any of the submitted proposals will not necessarily be accepted for an
   award of a contract by the Board.

   The District reserves the right, at its sole discretion, to waive variances in technical proposals provided
   such action is in the best interest of the District. Where the District waives minor variances in proposals,
   such waiver does not modify the RFP requirements or excuse the Contractor from full compliance with
   the RFP. Notwithstanding any minor variance, the District may hold any Contractor to strict compliance
    with the RFP.

    20.15 Right to Refuse Personnel
    The District reserves the right to refuse, at its sole discretion, any personnel provided by the Contractor.
    The District reserves the right to interview and approve all Contractor staff members.

    certified medical facility or lab. The Contractor will be responsible for all costs associated with background
    checks and drug testing. The Contractor shall obtain written permission from employees prior to releasing
    background check and drug test results to the District. The Contractor's staff may be subject to the

       20.17 Disclosure of Proposal Contents
       All proposals and other materials submitted in response to this RFP become the property of the District.
       _
       Selection or rejection of a proposal does not affect this right. Public disclosure of competitive proposals
       submitted to the District shall await conclusion of the negotiation process, but shall occur before the
       recommendation is finally approved by the Board. By submitting a proposal, the Contractor acknowledges
       and accepts that the contents of the proposal and associated documents will become open to public
       inspection.

       20.18 Proprietary Information
       Each proposal will become public record after the award of a contract unless the proposal or specific parts
       of the proposal can be shown to be exempt by law (Government Code Section 7931.000 et seq.). Each
       Contractor may clearly label part of a proposal as "CONFIDENTIAL" if the Contractor thereby agrees to
       indemnify and defend the District for honoring such a designation. The failure to so label any information
       that is released by t he District will constitute a complete waiver of all claims for damages caused by any
       release of the information.

       20.19 Consultant Participation
       The District reserves the right to share with any consultant of its choosing this RFP and proposal responses
       as it deems necessary. The District may, in its discretion utilize said consultant in connection with the
       proposal evaluation process.

       20.20 Severability
       If any provision of this RFP is declared by a court to be illegal or in conflict with any law, the validity of the
       remaining terms and provisions will not be affected; and, th e rights and obligations of the District and
       Contractors will be construed and enforced as if the RFP did not contain the particular provision held to
       be invalid.

       20.21 Execution of Final Contract
       The Contractor that receives the top score by the evaluation committee will be required to enter into a
       separate formal written contract approved by the Board. This RFP, including referenced attachments, will
       be incorporated into the final contract unless the RFP or provisions therein are excluded in the fin al
       written contract approved by the Board. A contract will not be binding or valid with the District unless and
       until it is approved by the District's Board of Directors and executed by authorized representatives of the
       District and of the Contractor.

       The formal written contract, which will be similar to the attached Sample Contract, will be prepared by
       the District and provided to the Contractor for review. The Contractor will be required to execute a formal
       written contract to be submitted to the Board for final approval within 14 ca lendar days from issuance of
       the Notice of Intent. Failure to comply may cause the District to negotiate a formal written contract with
       another Contractor recommended by the evaluation committee.

       Should the successful Contractor fail to execute the contract within 14 ca lendar days from the issuance of
       the Notice of Intent, the District and the Contractor will be released, without penalty, or further
       obligations other than any surviving obligations regarding confidentiality, and the District may, at its own
       discretion, extend a contract award to another Contractor whose proposal is considered suitable ahd
       demonstrates the next best value to the District.

ADAM A. HOUSE
  Fire Chief



  DATE:          May 22, 2025

  TO:            Board of Directors

  SUBJECT:       Measure 0 - General Obligation Bond Financing Plan


                                                  TOPIC

  The District's Board of Directors will be presented a Measure O financing plan to include a
  resolution (authorizing the issuance of bonds and approving a paying agent agreement, a
  notice of intention, a notice of sale, a preliminary official statement, and a continuing
  disclosure certificate) (the "Bond Resolution") , and a resolution approving a disclosure
  procedure (the "Disclosure Procedure Resolution").

                                            BACKGROUND

   On November 5, 2024, District voters approved Measure 0, authorizing the District to issue
   up to $415 million in general obligation bonds for capital projects, which the District plans to
   issue and commit over the next 1O years. The District anticipates three general obligation
   bond issuances; the first early in fiscal year (FY) 2025/26, followed by bond issuances
   anticipated in FY 2028/29 and FY 2031/32.

  The Board of Directors is considering two Resolutions authorizing the issuance and sale of
  the Sacramento Metropolitan Fire District (Sacramento and Placer Counties, California)
  General Obligation Bonds, Election of 2024, Series A (2025) (the "2025A GOs"). The purpose
  of the financing is to provide funds to finance the construction, improvements, and expansion
  of fire stations, training facilities, and various fire and emergency equipment (including
  vehicles and apparatus). The proceeds of the 2025A GOs will also pay the costs of issuance
  of the 2025A GOs. District staff have worked diligently with the financing team over the past
  several months to prepare the structure and documentation of the 2025A GOs for the Board's
  consideration.

                                              DISCUSSION

  The District will be issuing General Obligation Bonds in a par amount not-to-exceed $160
  million, which represents a portion of the total $415 million Measure O authorization. The
  2025A GOs will be issued as tax-exempt fixed-rate obligations that will pay principal annually
  and interest semi-annually for a term of approximately 30 years, with a final maturity of August
  1, 2055. The 2025A GOs will be structured to achieve level debt service, by bond year ending
  August 1st. The source of repayment of the 2025A GOs is an ad valorem tax that will be
  levied upon subject properties in the District. The 2025A GOs will be issued with a 10-year



                                  Serving Sacramento and Placer Counties

                                                                                                          P120
par optional call prov1s1on. Finally, it is anticipated that the 2025A GOs will price via a
competitive sale in mid-June and close on July 2, 2025.

Below is an estimate of the sources and uses of the proceeds of 2025A GOs, based upon
market conditions as of May 8, 2025. Please note these figures are preliminary and subject
to changes in market conditions until the pricing of the 2025A GOs.


                               Sources
                                   Bond Par Amount:             $160,000,000
                                   Premium:                       11,208,015
                               Total Sources:                   $171,208,015

                               Uses
                                   Project Fund:                $158,840,000
                                   Debt Service Fund:             11,208,015
                                   Cost of Issuance:                 360,000
                                   Underwriter's Discount:           800,000
                               Total Uses:                      $171,208,015



                               True Interest Cost                     4.46%
                               Average Annual Payments:          $10,419,960
                               Total Payments:                  $313,438,194

                               Final Maturity:                  August1, 2055
                               First Optional Call Date:        August 1,2035

                     Footnote: Based upon market conditions as of May 8, 2025. Preliminary and subject to final pricing
                     results.

Following are the documents submitted for approval through the Bond Resolution, as well as
key parameters for the sale of the 2025A GOs, including not-to-exceed par amount, borrowing
rate, among others. The Bond Resolution instructs District staff to complete the transaction,
based upon the parameters specified in the Bond Resolution. The Bond Resolution approves
the form and authorizes execution of the following documents:

   1. Notice of Intention
       The 2025A GOs are anticipated to be sold via a competitive method of sale. The
       Notice of Intention sets forth summary terms of the sale of the 2025A GOs and is
       published as required by law.

   2. Official Notice of Sale
       The 2025A GOs are anticipated to be sold via a competitive method of sale. The
       Official Notice of Sale sets forth the terms and conditions upon which underwriting
       firms will submit their competitive bid.

   3. Paying Agent Agreement
      The Paying Agent Agreement is between the District and U.S. Bank Trust Company,
      National Association, as paying agent. The Paying Agent Agreement establishes



                               Serving Sacramento and Placer Counties

                                                                                                                          P1 21
       U.S. Bank as the Paying Agent, Transfer Agent and Bond Registrar, and Custodian
       and Disbursing Agent in connection with the 2025A GOs.

   4. Continuing Disclosure Certificate
      The Continuing Disclosure Certificate is an undertaking by the District for the benefit
      of the investors in the 2025A GOs under which District agrees to provide annual
      updates regarding the District and its finances, in the form of the ACFR and updates
      to certain tables in the Official Statement

   5. Preliminary Official Statement ("POS")
      The POS serves as the primary disclosure document that summarizes the key credit
      features of the District. Potential investors will base their investment decision upon
      the information disclosed in the POS. While prepared and reviewed by third party
      consultants, the POS is ultimately the District's document and should be reviewed
      carefully for accuracy. Under federal securities laws, the Preliminary Official
      Statement must include all facts that would be material to an investor. Information is
      "material" if there is a substantial likelihood it would have actual significance in the
      deliberations of a reasonable investor when deciding whether to buy or sell
      securities. The proposed Resolution approves the POS, and delegates to staff (a)
      the ability to make additional changes if needed, and (b) to sign a certificate on
      behalf of the District that deems the POS final for purposes of the federal securities
      laws.

Additionally, the Disclosure Procedure Resolution approves a procedure that memorializes
practices and procedures in writing to ensure compliance by the District personnel with the
District's responsibilities under federal securities laws.

                                      FISCAL IMPACT

Because the expenses associated with the Measure O issuance are paid through the bonds
funds, there is no impact on the District's General Fund . The costs of issuance are estimated
to be $1 .16 million, paid from the 2025A GO proceeds and includes the costs associated with
the services provided by the municipal advisor, bond counsel, and rating agencies, plus the
estimated cost to transact the sale in the market (i.e., underwriter's discount).

                                   RECOMMENDATION

Adopt the two resolutions authorizing execution of the Measure O Financing Plan.


Submitted by:



Dave O'Toole                                       Adam A. House
Chief Financial Officer                            Fire Chief

   A RESOLUTION OF THE BOARD OF DIRECTORS OF THE SACRAMENTO
 METROPOLITAN FIRE DISTRICT AUTHORIZING THE ISSUANCE AND SALE OF
 THE DISTRICT'S GENERAL OBLIGATION BONDS, ELECTION OF 2024, SERIES
          A (2025), IN AN AMOUNT NOT TO EXCEED $160,000,000


       RESOLVED, by the Board of Directors (the "Board of Directors") of the
  Sacramento Metropolitan Fire District (the "District"), as follows:

       WHEREAS, a duly called special municipal election was held in the District on
  November 5, 2024, and thereafter canvassed pursuant to law;

           WHEREAS, at such election there was submitted to and approved by the requisite
  two-thirds (2/3) vote of the qualified electors of the District a question as to the issuance
  and sale of general obligation bonds of the District to finance the acquisition, improvement
  and upgrade of fire stations, facilities and real property, including (i) facilities, apparatus
  and equipment that support emergency lifesaving medical services, reduce 911 response
  times and maintain wildfire protection services, and (ii) replacing outdated stations, and
  (iii) a training facility and expansion project (the "Project"), in the maximum aggregate
  principal amount of $415,000,000 (the "Bonds") payable from the levy of an ad valorem
  tax against the taxable property in the District (the "Authorization");

         WHEREAS, pursuant to section 13925 at seq. of the Fire Protection District Act
  and Article 4.5, commencing with section 53506 of Chapter 3 of Part 1 of Division 2 of
  Title 5 of the California Government Code, the District is empowered to issue general
  obligation bonds;

          WHEREAS, the District wishes at this time to authorize the issuance and sale of
  the first series of general obligation bonds under the Authorization in the aggregate
  principal amount of not to exceed $160,000,000, its Sacramento Metropolitan Fire District
  (Sacramento and Placer Counties, California) General Obligation Bonds, Election of
  2024, Series A (2025) (the "Series A Bonds") for the purpose of raising moneys for the
  Project and other authorized costs;

       NOW THEREFORE BE IT RESOLVED, by the Board of Directors of the
  Sacramento Metropolitan Fire District, as follows:

                                                        ARTICLE I

                                            DEFINITIONS; AUTHORITY


Section 1.01. Definitions. The terms defined in this Section 1.01, as used and capitalized herein, shall, for all purposes
of this Resolution, have the meanings ascribed to them below, unless the context clearly requires some other meaning.

"Act" means section 13925 at seq. of the Fire Protection District Act and Article 4.5, commencing with section 53506 of
Chapter 3 of Part 1 of Division 2 of Title 5 of the California Government Code, as is in effect on the date of adoption
hereof and as amended hereafter.

"Articles," "Sections" and other subdivisions are to the corresponding Articles, Sections or subdivisions of this
Resolution, and the words "herein," "hereof," "hereunder" and other words of similar import refer to this Resolution
as a whole and not to any particular Article, Section or subdivision hereof.

"Authorized Investments" means the Sacramento County Investment Pool (or other investment pools of Sacramento
County into which the District may lawfully invest its funds), the Local Agency Investment Fund of the State, any
investment authorized pursuant to sections 16429.1 or 53601 of the California Government Code, and any investment
authorized in the Official Statement.

"Board" means the Board of Directors of the District.

"Bond Counsel" means any attorney or firm of attorneys nationally recognized for expertise in rendering opinions as to
the legality and tax exempt status of securities issued by public entities.

"Bond Register" means the registration books for the Series A Bonds maintained by the Paying Agent.

"Closing Date" means the date upon which there is an exchange of the Series A Bonds for the proceeds representing the
purchase of the Series A Bonds by the Original Purchaser.

"Code" means the Internal Revenue Code of 1986 as in effect on the date of issuance of the Series A Bonds or (except as
otherwise referenced herein) as it may be amended to apply to obligations issued on the date of issuance of the Series
A Bonds, together with applicable temporary and final regulations promulgated, and applicable official public
guidance published, under the Code.

"Continuing Disclosure Certificate" shall mean that certain Continuing Disclosure Certificate executed by the District
and dated the date of issuance and delivery of the Series A Bonds, as originally executed and as it may be amended
from time to time in accordance with the terms thereof.

"Costs of Issuance" means all items of expense directly or indirectly reimbursable to the District relating to the issuance,
execution and delivery of the Series A Bonds including, but not limited to, filing and recording costs, settlement costs,
printing costs, reproduction and binding costs, legal fees and charges, fees and expenses of the Paying Agent, financial
and other professional consultant fees, costs of obtaining credit ratings, fees for execution, transportation and
safekeeping of the Series A Bonds and charges and fees in connection with the foregoing.

 "Counties" means, collectively, Sacramento County, California, and Placer County, California.

 "Debt Service" means the scheduled amount of interest and amortization of principal payable on the Series A Bonds
 during the period of computation, excluding amounts scheduled during such period which relate to principal which
 has been retired before the beginning of such period.

"Director of Finance" means the Sacramento County Director of Finance.

"District Representative" means the Board President, the Board Vice President, the Fire Chief, the Chief Financial Officer,
the Chief Development Officer, the Controller or any other person authorized by resolution of the Board of Directors
of the District to act on behalf of the District with respect to this Resolution and the Series A Bonds.

"Fair Market Value" means the price at which a willing buyer would purchase the investment from a willing seller in a
bona fide, arm's length transaction (determined as of the date the contract to purchase or sell the investment becomes
binding) if the investment is traded on an established securities market (within the meaning of section 1273 of the
Code) and, otherwise, the term "Fair Market Value" means the acquisition price in a bona fide arm's length transaction
(as referenced above) if (i) the investment is a certificate of deposit that is acquired in accordance with applicable
regulations under the Code, (ii) the investment is an agreement with specifically negotiated withdrawal or
reinvestment provisions and a specifically negotiated interest rate (for example, a guaranteed investment contract, a
forward supply contract or other investment agreement) that is acquired in accordance with applicable regulations
under the Code, (iii) the investment is a United States Treasury Security-State and Local Government Series that is
acquired in accordance with applicable regulations of the United States Bureau of Public Debt, or (iv) any commingled
investment fund in which the District and related parties do not own more than a ten percent (10%) beneficial interest
therein if the return paid by the fund is without regard to the source of the investment.

"Federal Securities" means United States Treasury Bonds, bills or certificates of indebtedness or those for which the faith
and credit of the United States are pledged for the payment of principal and interest.

"I11for111atio11 Services" means the Electronic Municipal Market Access System (referred to as "EMMA"), a facility of the
Municipal Securities Rulemaking Board (at http://emma.msrb.org) or, in accordance with then current guidelines of
the Securities and Exchange Commission, such other addresses and/or such other national information services
providing information with respect to called bonds as the District may designate to the Paying Agent.

"Interest Payment Date" means with respect to interest, February 1 and August 1 of each year commencing on February
1, 2026, and with respect to principal, August 1, of each year commencing on August 1 in such year as shall be set forth
in the Notice of Sale.

"Municipa_l Adviso,/' means KNN Public Finance, LLC, Berkeley, California, as Municipal Advisor to the District in
connection with the issuance of the Series A Bonds.

"Notice of Sale" means the official notice of sale relating to the Series A Bonds.

"Office" means the office or offices of the Paying Agent for the payment of the Series A Bonds and the administration
of its duties hereunder. Initially, the Office of the Paying Agent is One California Street, Suite 1000, San Francisco,
California. The Office may be re-designated from time to time under written notice filed with the District by the Paying
Agent.

"Original Purchaser" means the first purchaser of the Series A Bonds from the District.

"Outstanding" means, when used as of any particular time with reference to Series A Bonds, all Series A Bonds except:

(a) Series A Bonds theretofore canceled by the Paying Agent or surrendered to the Paying Agent for cancellation;

(b) Series A Bonds paid or deemed to have been paid wi~in the meaning of Section 9.02 hereof; and

(c) Series A Bonds in lieu of or in substitution for which other Series A Bonds shall have been authorized, executed,
issued and delivered by the District pursuant to this Resolution.

"Owner" or "Bondowner" mean any person who shall be the registered owner of any Outstanding Series A Bond.

Date, by and between the District and the Paying Agent.

"Principal Office" means the principal corporate trust office of the Paying Agent in San Francisco, California.

"Regulations" means tempora1y and permanent regulations promulgated under the Code.

"Resolution" means this Resolution, including all amendments hereto and supplements hereof which are duly adopted
by the Board of Directors from time to time in accordance herewith.

"Securities Depositories" means The Depository Trust Company, 55 Water Street, 50th Floor, New York, NY 10041-0099,
Attention: Call Notification Department, Fax (212) 855-7232; and, in accordance with then current guidelines of the
Securities and Exchange Commission, such other addresses and/or such other securities depositories as the District
may designate to the Paying Agent.

"Series A Bonds" means the Sacramento Metropolitan Fire District (Sacramento and Placer Counties, California) General
Obligation Bonds, Election of 2024, Series A (2025), issued and at any time Outstanding pursuant to this Resolution.

"S11pplemental Resol11tio11" means any resolution supplemental to or amendatory of this Resolution, adopted by the
District in accordance with Article VIII hereof.

"Term Bonds" means those Series A Bonds for which mandatory redemption dates have been established pursuant to
the Notice of Sale.

"Written Request of the District" means an instrument in writing signed by the District Representative or by any other
officer of the District duly authorized by the District and listed on a Written Request of the District for that purpose.

Section 1.02. Authority for this Resolution. This Resolution is entered into pursuant to the provisions of the Act.
